EVIDENCE (file:line in hive unless noted):
- AUTONOMY+REPOS (WIRED): scanner daemon `hive civilization daemon --issue-scan-interval <d>` spawns a background ticker goroutine (cmd/hive/main.go:1353-1362, cmd/hive/factory_issue_scan_scanner.go:72-134) that polls GitHub across a repo LIST configured via repeatable --issue-scan-repo flags OR --issue-scan-registry (reads repos.json) (factory.go:187-195,305-311). Selects top-ranked candidate with `cc:pr-ready` label (issue_intake.go:229,313-343), queues as factory.run.requested. Guardrails ALL wired: --issue-scan-one-active (factory_issue_scan_scanner.go:166-174), --issue-scan-max-duration hard cap (76-79), --issue-scan-kill-switch file checked every cycle (229-240), --issue-scan-max-new-runs (91-93), every run at AuthorityLevelRequired (212-213); --issue-scan-interval cannot combine with --approve-* (factory.go:234-238). NUANCE: scan+selection is autonomous, but progressing a run through stages to a ready PR fully unattended depends on stage-runner flags being wired + approval config. ONE issue per run (one-active), not batch.
- LIFECYCLE+POSSESSION (WIRED): 7 stages (issue_intake.go:628-711): research_issue_and_repo_context(design) -> debate_with_correct_civic_roles(CFADA) -> select_and_design_approach(design) -> implement_on_branch(code) -> run_adversarial_review(CFAR) -> drive_blockers_to_zero(blockers/debug) -> surface_ready_for_Human_result_PR(ready). NO 'IAR' stage exists in code — Michael to clarify what IAR denotes (open).

## 2026-07-01 · ??

[MARKER: wiki-ingest-ops-design · commit wiki@86b4257 · 2026-07-01] Design decision — transpara-ai/wiki, branch feat/per-ingestion-operations. Brainstormed "Item 1" of a wiki-improvement session with Michael: per-ingestion operations for the Karpathy-style LLM wiki (raw/ → LLM-compiled wiki/*.md → dist/ static site, served loopback :8787 by compile/ingest_server.py). Committed spec: docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-01-per-ingestion-operations-design.md.

Locked decisions:
1. Rules are a PER-INGESTION operation mode (add | replace | remove), NOT a persistent per-topic policy (Michael reversed his first answer). No scheduler ever acts destructively; destructive intent is always human-in-the-moment.
2. All three ops are append-only SUPERSESSION over the Event substrate (grounds in the 2026-06-16 ontology spec: Event is append-only, no Update/Delete, "Revise = supersede"). No rm/overwrite of raw/ or wiki/ anywhere. This spec realizes "Sub-project A / Update Now" that the ontology spec deferred.
3. Replace = swap raw (deterministic, instant, air-gap-safe) + immediate recompile. Engine = Claude, ONE-CLICK authority-gated (mirrors deploy-authorization.json), degrading to honest-"stale" when offline/unauthorized. Rationale: the codebase deliberately avoided LLM synthesis for "expensive+autonomous spend" — the one-click gate removes the "silent"+"autonomous" words while keeping synthesis.
4. Remove = cascading RECONCILIATION, not delete. Tombstone the topic (retired stub); attempt in-context re-resolution of inbound [[wikilinks]]; truly-broken refs → mark dangling-pending + enqueue link-source raw for reprocessing. Run to closure.
5. Prime invariant (Michael): MAXIMUM REFERENTIAL INTEGRITY AT ALL TIMES. Achieved by a two-layer split — Layer 1 deterministic integrity pass (LLM-free, instant, always-on, holds even offline/mid-cascade) + Layer 2 authority-gated reconciliation (restores completeness). Key insight: integrity = what the graph CLAIMS, not when reprocessing finishes; a visibly-marked "dangling-pending" edge does NOT violate integrity, a live-rendering-but-resolving-to-nothing edge does. Edge-state machine: valid | cleanly-removed | dangling-pending, with fail-closed rendering (live only when proven valid; no default: branch renders live).

North star for the whole wiki (Michael, 2026-07-01): instructive, educational, prescriptive, easy for a HUMAN to digest. Still pending: Item 2 = front-page redesign AND a REAL re-think of the convoluted civilizationArc metrics/tracking; Item 3 = advisory memo on plugins/skills/MCP servers.

## 2026-07-01 · ??

[MARKER: wiki-arc-metrics-redesign · commit wiki@a2ebcf2 · 2026-07-01] Design decision — transpara-ai/wiki, branch feat/arc-metrics-redesign. Item 2b of the wiki-improvement brainstorm with Michael: the REAL re-think of the convoluted civilizationArc metrics. Committed spec: docs/superpowers/specs/2026-07-01-arc-metrics-redesign-design.md.

INTROSPECTIVE FINDING: the convolution was a MISSING PURPOSE, not sloppy code — the arc tried to be 5 things at once. Fix starts by choosing ONE purpose.

Locked decisions:
- Purpose (Michael) = "WHERE ARE WE, AND WHAT'S NEXT?" — current-state/frontier read; history is secondary context. Everything else falls out of this.
- First-class pieces (Michael) = Work + Gates on a PHASE backbone. Decision/Event/Goal/Artifact demote to detail-on-click.
- ONE status vocabulary (ontology §1.5 finally enforced): future→planned→active→done + blocked overlay + blocked_reason enum {gate,resource,authority,recovery,dependency}. DELETE parallel statuses boundary_status/go_live_revalidation/evidence_state/authority_state.
- Status is DERIVED FAIL-CLOSED from evidence-backed gate acceptance criteria[], never asserted. Rollup: done ONLY if all criteria done; blocked wins; else active/planned/future. Makes the Gate-K contradiction structurally impossible.
- Distinct scopes → distinct gates (Michael): Gate-K(pre-live)=done behind frontier; Gate-K(go-live)=blocked ahead = "what's next".
- Evidence-basis + freshness stamped on EVERY piece (Michael): evidence-derived where possible (live PRs/artifacts/merge via inflight.py), hand-authored+stamped otherwise; reconstructed pieces (Feb genesis) stamped reconstructed. Kills stale-while-green structurally.
- Single plane: fold executionPlan in (was duplicate worklist); evidence first-class (not liveReaderEvidence side table). Referential integrity ENFORCED (fail build on orphan phase/gate/dep refs; reject parallel-status fields; gate must have criteria[]; single source of truth for gate families). now-frontier DERIVED.

DIAGNOSIS (Explore agent, receipts): 4 parallel un-reconciled planes (items[]/liveReaderEvidence/executionPlan/inflight); ~9 status vocabularies; smoking gun Gate-K carries status:done + boundary_status + go_live_revalidation:blocked + a prose note explaining its own contradiction (a FAIL-OPEN bug — green while go-live unmet); arc data diverged from civilizationOntology.js (gates carry unchecked fields; sprint refs unvalidated; gate families hardcoded twice).

LAYOUT: freshness header + now-panel ("you are here": current phase, active work w/ evidence stamps, next gate w/ criteria checklist + fail-closed rollup) + phase spine (frontier marked, past collapses) + one-status legend. 6 grouping modes → the spine IS the view.

MIGRATION = NET DELETION: rewrite civilizationArcData.js to unified schema; DELETE most of civilizationArcNav.js (~56KB, mode toggles); simplify/replace civilizationArcLayout+Draw (now-panel+spine are near-static HTML, no ordinal SVG engine); KEEP+TIGHTEN civilizationOntology.js as validator; inflight.py becomes the derived-status source; rewire build_site.py arc_page + stats.py. Air-gap, no LLM in arc path.

This realigns the arc with the 2026-06-16 ontology spec it drifted from; same fail-closed + referential-integrity + single-source-of-truth principles as Item 1 (per-ingestion ops, branch feat/per-ingestion-operations, marker wiki-ingest-ops-design).

[OB-CHECKPOINT marker=2026-07-01T-statespace-refactor-checkpoint · session=wiki-improvement+TLC+statemachine] Long session with Michael, resuming in a fresh context. PIVOT POINT: about to DESIGN the canonical work-state-machine refactor (the root fix for state-space ambiguity), with an agreed model-role split.

THE DECISION (settled, evidence-grounded, non-political): for the state-machine refactor — **Claude DESIGNS + does CFAR (code review); Codex does CFADA (design review) + IMPLEMENTS the plumbing; Michael authorizes + merges.** Rationale: (1) DF-V4.0-ADR-001 (accepted) already assigns Stage-2 implement=Codex, Stage-3 review=Claude; (2) this session showed Claude's comparative advantage is design/adversarial-analysis and Codex's CFADA caught a fail-open lane Claude authored (secret-scan C3) — proving reviewer-independence is the load-bearing safeguard; (3) NO provable evidence Codex out-implements Claude at Go — the split is doctrine+role-fit+independence, NOT a capability claim. Precondition: Claude must produce an AIRTIGHT test-first TLC design packet (bounds model-transfer loss).

THE ROOT CAUSE (systematic-debugging, code-proven) of state-space ambiguity: **There is no canonical, typed state machine for "the state of a unit of work."** Evidence: (a) the Work Graph (work/pkg) has NO state-machine type — task status is a BARE STRING (hive/pkg/hive/civilization_assembly_projection.go:1802-1826, string-compared to work.StatusCreated); (b) ~40+ independent *State/*Status/*Phase/*Stage/*Blocker Go types scattered across work/hive/eventgraph; (c) GitHub labels are yet another un-typed, human-set power-set, derived from none of them. So illegal/contradictory states (e.g. cc:pr-ready ∧ cc:pr-deferred) are representable BY CONSTRUCTION, resolved only fail-closed at read time — violating the hive's OWN standard "make illegal states unrepresentable." Same disease as the arc (Item 2b) one layer down. Answers the 3 questions: not a certificate (asserted strings), not a bijection (40 lossy projections, illegal combos representable), can't drive TLC (CFADA/IADA/IAR aren't states anywhere — grep: hive runtime has IADA=0 CFADA=0 IAR=0 CFAR=1-string).

THE TARGET ARCHITECTURE (root-directed, to be designed via TLC): (1) ONE canonical typed work-state machine — states + transition function, illegal transitions unrepresentable by type; (2) single source of truth = the EventGraph append-only fold (ontology's Event-substrate; state = fold); (3) EVERY projection derived from the fold — GitHub labels, PR statuses, the arc, the console — a label can't contradict state because it's computed, never independently set; (4) the TLC gates become named states/transitions in that machine (semver→design→IADA→CFADA→authorize→code→IAR→CFAR→ready→merged) so the runtime cycles TLC because TLC IS the machine, and CFADA/IADA/IAR finally exist as states; (5) collapse the 40+ parallel types into it. Scope = EPIC (eventgraph/work/hive + label taxonomy + governance-gates + docs); changes gate semantics + authority → cc:protected-action, human-authority-gated, MUST be decomposed.

NEXT ACTION (fresh session): invoke superpowers:brainstorming → design the canonical work-state machine + its decomposition → write a test-first TLC design packet (Claude authors) → Codex CFADA → Michael AuthorityDecision → Codex implements → Claude CFAR → Michael merges. Do NOT start code before the AuthorityDecision.

PARKED/PRIOR WORK this session (all transpara-ai/wiki unless noted, NO PRs, NO merges):
- Item 1 of the wiki BUILD = offline secret-scan pre-commit hook + CI gate. Parked at DESIGN v0.2.0 (branch feat/wiki-secret-scan-hook, commit 524fc13). semver✓ IADA✓ CFADA-round-1✓ (4 blockers repaired). ROOT CAUSE (code-proven, corrects the earlier "no state machine" framing): NOT absence but FRAGMENTATION — a good typed nucleus already exists (work.TaskStatus 14 states work/store.go:26 + canTransitionTask work/store.go:2120) among ~43 parallel *State/*Status reps (>=5 hand-rolled transition guards), degraded to a BARE STRING at the hive projection (civilization_assembly_projection.go:1802) and shadowed by LegacyTaskStatus (work/store.go:61). Gate-outcome vocab already exists in JSON schema (cfada/cfar-result.schema.json: pass|blocked|fail|waived, requires_human_authority).

DESIGN DECISIONS SETTLED WITH MICHAEL THIS SESSION (all via brainstorming, one Q at a time):
1. ONE NESTED machine (not flat, not two siblings): top-level governance-lifecycle macro-states = TLC gates; work.TaskStatus execution FSM nests INSIDE the Coding macro-state only (Exec=None elsewhere). Composite UnitState={Macro, Option[Exec], Option[BlockReason], Superseded bool} with construction invariant Exec.isSome <=> Macro==Coding => illegal states unrepresentable by type.
2. 8 macro-states on the spine + terminal Denied (9 total): Intake->Designing->DesignAudit(CFADA)->AwaitingAuth(authorize)->Coding->CodeReview(CFAR)->Ready->Merged; Denied for authority denial.
3. IADA/IAR are ACTIVITIES (not macro-states); their ZERO-BLOCKER result is a FAIL-CLOSED precondition to enter the cross-family counterpart (Michael's refinement: zero-blocker to progress to cross-family).
4. Build order chosen: Foundation->derive->gates = SP0->SP1->SP3->SP2->SP4->SP5 (each its own semver->design->CFADA->authority->implement->CFAR->merge arc). Decomposition SP0-SP5 recorded in the packet.
5. Auto-advance on certified: work.task.certified auto-advances Coding->CodeReview (Michael chose over request-guarded). Consequences baked in: certified subsumes IAR-complete; work.task.certified is a macro-transition trigger (reducer folds work.task.* too — cross-layer coupling, flagged RR2 for CFADA); cfar.blocked returns to Coding and REOPENS/supersedes certification (work.task.reopened). Certification-integrity (certified unreachable without verified) is AC8 = the load-bearing property auto-advance leans on.
6. GATE POLICY (Michael: "EVERY gate except CFAR is optional, but failed in the Selected (safe) state" — I confirmed the reading, he confirmed): every gate DEFAULTS to failed (fail-closed); flips to passed ONLY on explicit proven pass; skip != pass (skipped optional gate stays failed, projected as skipped not passed); CFAR is IRREDUCIBLY required, not configurable, admits no skip. Progression guard = allowlist/default-deny (pass OR (optional AND recorded skip); else deny). Aligns with prior Build-G GatePolicy (4 optional gates {IADA,CFADA,authorize,IAR}, fail-closed default).
7. SAFETY reconciliation (I surfaced, he confirmed): optional lifecycle authorize gate != authority for protected actions — protected-action guard stays SEPARATELY fail-closed (R9/AC10); human merge stays ALWAYS required.
8. Typed AuthorityDecision {outcome, bounded Scope, Exclusions, StopConditions, ResidualRisk} replaces authority.Resolution{Approved bool} (authority.go:30).

PACKET CONTENT: test-first, house-style (Requirements R1-R10; full transition table edge->driving-event->fail-closed-guard; gate model; 14 Acceptance Criteria each with verification_method+risk_class; 14 named Test Cases covering full MacroState x Event domain + every gate x {unset,blockers>0,missing,error,passed,skipped}; two Gate Predicates satisfied-only-when; Stop Conditions; Non-Authorizations; Role/Process; Authorization Packet; RR1-RR4). Self-review fixed 2 gaps: Ready->Merged guard now requires fresh exact-head CFAR pass + human approval (was merge fail-open); IADA/IAR<->CFADA/CFAR policy coupling clarified.

THE 7 BLOCKERS (all confirmed real):
1. PACKAGE PLACEMENT NOT BUILDABLE (circular dep): packet put SP0 in eventgraph/go/pkg/worklifecycle AND embedded work.TaskStatus, but work->eventgraph already (work/go.mod); eventgraph has NO work dep. Embedding => eventgraph must import work = reverse/circular dep; AC14 zero-behavior-change not credible. FIX: relocate SP0 to work (work/pkg/worklifecycle), which already imports eventgraph and owns TaskStatus.
2. CFADA SKIP LANE ILLEGAL FOR GOVERNED/PROTECTED CLASS: cfada.skipped advances Designing->AwaitingAuth when CFADA optional, but the standard REQUIRES CFADA for gate-semantics/authority/EventGraph-truth/Hive-APIs/Work-runtime/cross-repo (07-cfar-cfada-...:147-165,301-304). SP0 gave the skip mechanism but not the classification making governed CFADA non-skippable = fail-open for exactly this class. FIX: add GovernanceClass input; skip valid ONLY for proven non-governed/prototype; governed/protected/unknown/missing -> deny skip (gate REQUIRED). Touches Michael's "every gate except CFAR optional" -> refine to class-gated optional (honors his "failed in the Selected safe state").
3. authority.skipped ADVANCES PROTECTED WORK TO CODING: even with R9/AC10 (protected ACTION separately gated), the macro-state still CLAIMS Coding without authority; operator surfaces/reducers read Coding as implementation-authorized. FIX: authority.skipped invalid for cc:protected-action/human-gated units (same class-gating as #2); governed Coding reachable only via authority.granted.
4. READY CAN HOLD FAILED/STALE CFAR: Ready|ready.marked->Ready re-arms CFAR to failed while macro stays Ready = leaks "ready" before fresh pass. FIX: Ready reachable ONLY via cfar.passed at exact CURRENT head; any head change / ready re-arm returns unit to CodeReview for fresh exact-head CFAR. No stale-CFAR-in-Ready. (My self-review fixed the merge guard but left the state name overloaded.)
5. ILLEGAL Blocked+Ready STILL REPRESENTABLE: composite has independent Blocked overlay on ANY non-terminal incl Ready; R2 forbids Blocked&&Ready but AC1 only checked Exec-vs-Macro. Macro=Ready+Blocked=Some and Macro=Coding+Exec=ready+Blocked=Some both representable = recreates the bool illegal-combo the packet claims to kill. FIX: cross-field construction invariants over Macro x Exec x overlays; Blocked overlay restricted to active states (Designing/DesignAudit/AwaitingAuth/Coding/CodeReview), not Ready/Merged/Denied; SP0 Exec vocab defined WITHOUT its own ready/blocked (so no contradiction with overlay).
6. CFAR-BLOCKED REOPEN CONFLICTS WITH WORK TaskStatus: packet nests work.TaskStatus and needs cfar.blocked to return certified->non-certified, but work StatusCertified is TERMINAL (work/store.go:2167-2168), only Verified->Certified edge (:2192-2193), Reopen is legacy-completion-only (:555-585), GetStatus ignores reopen (:792-810). Return edge unimplementable without changing Work lifecycle => breaks AC14. FIX: SP0 defines its OWN minimal exec sub-vocab {implementing,self_reviewed,verified,certified} with NON-terminal certified; work.TaskStatus reuse becomes an ADAPTER deferred to SP1. Touches Michael's "nest work.TaskStatus" -> CODE-FORCED; intent preserved (exec nests in Coding; auto-advance on certified; cfar.blocked returns).
7. AC2 FULL-DOMAIN UNDER-SPECIFIED: real reducer domain is not MacroState x Event — also Exec, Blocked, Superseded, GovernanceClass, per-gate {policy,state}, artifacts, reviewer-family, head-SHA, internal-review-results, read-errors, authority-decision-content. Hidden dims are where fail-open/stale/skip-as-pass hide. FIX: define full event algebra + state/config product incl unknown/missing/read-error payloads; test the full product with default-deny; fix gate-predicate "total over MacroState x Event" claim.
+ RR5 citation drift: canTransitionTask is work/store.go:2163 (packet said :2120); Approved bool at authority.go:33 (said :30). Fix receipts.

TWO REPAIRS TOUCH MICHAEL'S PRIOR DECISIONS (flag before big rewrite): (a) #2/#3 governed-class refinement to "every gate optional" — optional only where non-governed/prototype, governed/unknown->required/deny (MORE fail-safe, honors his "failed in safe state" + canon); (b) #6 exec independence — SP0 defines own exec vocab, work.TaskStatus becomes SP1 adapter (code-forced by terminal certified; intent preserved). NON-blocking note from Codex: reuse hive's newer fail-closed protected-action vocab (hive/pkg/safety, hive/pkg/hive/authority_policy.go) instead of a weaker optional lifecycle skip.

PLAN: repair all 7 fixing the CLASS not the instance -> bump packet v0.1.0->v0.2.0 -> commit -> RE-RUN CFADA (round 2) -> loop to 0 blockers -> THEN stop for Michael AuthorityDecision. Asking Michael to confirm the governed-class refinement (a) before the rewrite since it refines his explicit directive. NO code before AuthorityDecision. transpara-ai only, feat branch feat/canonical-work-state-machine-sp0-design, local only (no push/PR/merge).

THE 3 ROUND-2 BLOCKERS (all valid):
1. GovernanceClass has NO authoritative assignment rule. Skip allowlist trusts Class==non_governed_prototype but WHO sets the class + HOW deferred to SP3 => a supplied/mis-derived class can skip CFADA/authority. Standard requires non-governed classification recorded WITH A REASON; absent/uncertain -> gate required (07-cfar-cfada:206-210). FIX: define SP0 CLASSIFIER CONTRACT now (fail-closed): cc:protected-action/human-gated -> governed_protected; absent/unreadable/conflicting/uncertain -> unknown (deny skip); non_governed_prototype accepted ONLY from recorded issue/PR evidence per standard. Add source-evidence x class tests. (This packet is itself cc:protected-action => classifies as governed_protected => CFADA non-skippable for it = self-consistent.)
2. Ready can remain STALE after a head change with NO folded event. UnitState has no reviewed-head/current-head binding; only exit is an explicit head.changed/ready.marked event; if a new commit lands and no event appended, fold still returns Ready = violates stale-head rule (07-cfar-cfada:233-234). FIX (deep + on-thesis): bind CFAR evidence to reviewed_head, carry current_head as projection input, DERIVE Ready only when reviewed_head==current_head; mismatch -> CodeReview/error regardless of events. Ready is DERIVED not HELD (the design's own derive-don't-hold thesis applied to itself). Add test: current head changes w/ no lifecycle event -> projection returns CodeReview not Ready.
3. ExecState table has OVERLAPPING successors for exec.certified: the exec.* wildcard row (stay Coding) overlaps the specific exec.certified row (->CodeReview) = non-unique successor, violates AC2. ALSO cfar.blocked from CodeReview says supersede "ExecState certified->implementing" but under I1 Exec cannot exist in CodeReview. FIX: replace exec.* wildcard with an EXPLICIT ExecState sub-FSM table (implementing->self_reviewed->verified->certified, each a specific row); exec.certified is the UNIQUE auto-advance (only from Exec=verified) Coding->CodeReview; cfar.blocked constructs a fresh (Macro=Coding, Exec=implementing) from history/evidence, not by mutating a non-existent in-CodeReview Exec.

PLAN: repair all 3 (targeted, v0.2.0->v0.3.0) -> commit -> CFADA round 3 -> loop to 0 -> THEN checkpoint (verified OB + bootstrap) + hand Michael a bounded AuthorityRequest. No code before AuthorityDecision. Branch feat/canonical-work-state-machine-sp0-design, docs repo, local only. Progress: r1=7 blockers, r2=3 blockers, converging.

[Open Brain marker: 2026-07-02T-demo-stack-up-worktasks-slow] Demo stack brought up for tonight's Mission Control demo (nucbuntu, 2026-07-02 ~13:20 WEST) + two operational discoveries in transpara-ai/work's work-server.

STACK STATE (all verified by curl, not assumed): hive-postgres-1 healthy (docker). hive-ops-api ALREADY ran as user service on 127.0.0.1:8085 with HIVE_OPS_CATALOG=/Transpara/transpara-ai/repos/hive/catalog-mixed.yaml and 1m hot reload — serves /api/hive/operator-projection (11 models, 9 role assignments: allocator/guardian/spawner→gemma4, cto/implementer→gpt-5.5, planner→claude-sonnet-4-6, reviewer/strategist→deepseek-v4-pro; all Auto · inferred provenance) and the civilization assembly projection. site.service (PORT=80, drop-in 10-hive-ops.conf wires HIVE_OPS_API_BASE_URL=http://127.0.0.1:8085 + key) REDEPLOYED from branch feat/mission-control-config-view via make deploy (health 200, started 13:13) — the deployed binary now includes PR #201's /console/config. Console status: Health=live/0 agents (honest, no run in flight); Intake=live with 3 real cards (docs#226, operation#26, operation#45); Config=live, catalog-mixed, hot-reload; Kanban=honest unavailable (see below). hive agent runtime NOT started (a civilization run needs Michael's --idea and spends tokens; command ready: cd repos/hive && go run ./cmd/hive civilization run --human Michael --catalog catalog-mixed.yaml --idea "...").

DISCOVERY 1 — orphaned work-server held :8080 across systemd restart. work-server.service runs `/snap/bin/go run ./cmd/work-server`; on `systemctl --user restart` the go-run PARENT died but the compiled CHILD binary (~/.cache/go-build/.../work-server, pid 4315, up since Jun 30) survived as an orphan still bound to *:8080 → every new service instance exited 1 (address in use) in a 10s crash-restart loop with NO app-level error line in journal. Fix: kill the orphan pid; systemd auto-restart then bound cleanly. LESSON: units that ExecStart `go run` don't kill their compiled children on stop — either use the built binary in ExecStart or KillMode=control-group check; when a service crash-loops with silent journal, check `ss -tlnp` for a port squatter first.

DISCOVERY 2 — work-server GET /tasks takes ~12s and breaks its consumers. Consistent 11.95-12.01s across runs (fresh process, so NOT stale connections); pg_stat_activity during flight shows an active full event-stream SELECT — handler re-folds all 21,915 events (17MB) per request (~2ms/event; smells like per-event verification or N+1). Site's obsWorkClient timeout is hardcoded 5s (site graph/observatory.go:29) → /console/kanban and /ops work views render honest-unavailable "Client.Timeout exceeded". This is PRE-EXISTING (event volume grew past the timeout), NOT caused by PR #201; console fail-closed behavior is working as designed. Deliberately did NOT shim a caching proxy for the demo — a 30s-stale cache would be stamped live-as-of-fetch by the site (console_kanban.go comment: a successful fetch IS current), i.e. fake freshness, violating the honest-staleness contract the demo is selling. Spawned follow-up task chip task_93b5d6b8 "Fix work-server /tasks 12s full-stream replay" (profile, then snapshot/incremental fold; TLC applies). Demo framing: Kanban's unavailable state is a live demonstration of no-fabrication.

NO merges ever (Michael's). transpara-ai only, never upstream/lovyou-ai. Open Brain capture w/ read-back per milestone. GOTCHA: any Bash arg text containing the codex review command + quotes trips cross-family-review-guard.sh — use --body-file for PR/issue bodies mentioning it.

[MARKER: wiki-secret-scan-cfada-r2-repaired · commit wiki@bcd040a · 2026-07-02T00:00Z] TLC design loop progress — transpara-ai/wiki, branch feat/wiki-secret-scan-hook (local only, not pushed). Secret-scan hook design packet: CFADA round 2 (Codex, on v0.2.0 head 524fc13) returned FAIL — 4 blockers + 1 major, judging three of the four round-1 repairs (C2/C3/C4) only PARTIAL. Root class across all four blockers: an outcome lane not provably deny-by-default (the hive#131 spiral pattern recurring in design space).

Findings → repairs (committed as v0.3.0 @ bcd040a):
- B1 CI history escape (hook bypass + commit secret + remove before final diff ⇒ CI passed): scan domain now = union of blobs across EVERY commit in merge-base(<base>,HEAD)..HEAD, rename detection off, fetch-depth 0, unresolvable ref/blob ⇒ block. New test test_secret_added_then_removed_in_history_blocked.
- B2 fingerprint per blob not per finding (one reviewed false positive covered an unreviewed sibling secret of the same rule in the same blob): key gains match_sha256 = SHA-256 of the exact matched byte span. New test test_allowlist_entry_does_not_cover_sibling_findings.
- B3 binary "skip-with-reason" = reasoned pass = fail-open: binary blobs now BLOCK by default, clearable only by fingerprint after manual review; CLASS FIX — the scanner outcome vocabulary is closed to {pass, allowlisted, block}; "skip" removed from the domain entirely (AC7 rewritten).
- B4 detector contract was regex sketches: §3.2 now has exact anchored regexes, normalization rules (UTF-8 errors=replace, whitespace-tolerant JSON), honest rule names (aws-access-key-id, github-token incl. github_pat_, openai-sk-key incl. sk-proj-), defined entropy thresholds (generic-assignment ≥3.5 bits/char len≥16; high-entropy backstop ≥4.5 bits/char len≥32 — hex charset caps at 4.0 so git SHAs/UUIDs are negative by construction), grammar-bound fixtures (AC8: a fixture satisfied via a different rule doesn't count).
- M1 allowlist erosion ungoverned: schema now mandates reason+owner+reviewed_by+reviewed_on+expires_on (≤180 days, renewal only by re-review); validated every run; malformed/expired ⇒ scan BLOCKS (new AC10 + test_allowlist_schema_and_expiry_enforced).

Audit-trail honesty: round-1 appendix dispositions corrected from "FIXED" to "partial → completed at v0.3.0" where round 2 falsified them; new round-2 appendix table added. ACs now AC1–AC10.

CFADA round 3 (Codex) launched against head bcd040a — loop continues until 0 blockers, then STOP for Michael's AuthorityDecision (§7 bounded scope: wiki-only, draft-PR-only, no merge) before any implementation. Related markers: wiki-secret-scan-tlc-checkpoint (the v0.2.0 checkpoint), wiki-ingest-ops-design, wiki-front-page-vision-board.

CFADA round 3 on transpara-ai/wiki branch feat/wiki-secret-scan-hook head bcd040a4264e50459db45fdc4d74e1f198159fb0 failed the v0.3.0 secret-scan hook design. Key blockers found: §3 uses `git diff-tree -r --no-renames` without merge handling, so merge-commit changes are not enumerated; §7 authorizes only adding a separate `secret-scan` job while live main protection currently requires `Build & Test` and `cross-family-adversarial-review`, so the new job would not be an enforced gate; §3 distinct-blob union conflicts with §3.1 path-bound per-finding allowlist; §3.1 binary/oversized whole-blob fingerprint clearance contradicts the no-blob/no-skip claim; §3.2 source regexes use escaped alternation such as `AKIA\|ASIA`, making AWS and generic-assignment fixtures fail if implemented as the stated Python regex; and submodule/gitlink inputs are not denied by default.

## 2026-07-02 · ??

[MARKER: wiki-secret-scan-cfada-r3-repaired · commit wiki@1364d45 · 2026-07-02] TLC design loop — transpara-ai/wiki, branch feat/wiki-secret-scan-hook (local only). CFADA round 3 (Codex, on v0.3.0 head bcd040a) returned FAIL — 6 blockers + 1 major. Round 3 escalated audit quality by verifying claims against the LIVE repo (branch protection, ci.yml), catching a hollow-enforcement claim no doc-only read would find.

Findings → repairs (committed v0.4.0 @ 1364d45):
- R3-B1: `git diff-tree -r` emits nothing for merge commits — a secret introduced in a merge/conflict resolution evaded AC3. Fix: `-m` diffs each merge against EACH parent; test_secret_in_merge_commit_blocked.
- R3-B2 (the standout): §7 forbade branch-protection changes while calling a NEW separate secret-scan CI job "the real gate" — but live main protection requires only "Build & Test" + "cross-family-adversarial-review" (verified myself via gh api, 2026-07-02), so a separate job could NEVER block a merge. Decorative gate. Fix: the scan runs as a STEP INSIDE the required Build & Test job; test_scan_step_lives_in_required_build_and_test_job asserts the wiring.
- R3-B3: "union of distinct blobs" contradicted the path-bound allowlist key (dedup erased path occurrences → one reviewed path could cover identical content at an unreviewed path). Fix: scan/report unit = (canonical_path, blob_sha256) OCCURRENCE; blob dedup allowed only as internal optimization; test_allowlist_entry_does_not_cover_other_paths.
- R3-B4: v0.3.0's binary "whole-blob fingerprint" clearance was the skip lane RENAMED — one entry cleared arbitrary unscanned blob content while §3.1 claimed per-finding scope. Fix: two honestly distinct record types in .secretsallow — text `fingerprint` (per-finding, match_sha256) vs `blob_review` (whole-blob human attestation, explicitly scoped as such, NEVER valid for text blobs); test_blob_review_rejected_for_text_blobs.
- R3-B5 (embarrassing+instructive): I escaped pipes as \| inside markdown table cells then labeled the column "Exact grammar (Python re)" — in Python re, \| is a LITERAL pipe, so the stated fixtures could not match the stated grammars. Fix: grammars moved verbatim into a fenced code block as the authoritative contract; table carries fixtures only. LESSON: never put load-bearing regexes in markdown table cells.
- R3-B6: gitlinks (mode 160000) aren't blobs — a submodule pointer + .gitmodules bypassed the blob scanner. Fix: gitlink or .gitmodules change ⇒ block, NO clearance lane in v1; symlinks (120000) scanned as text; test_gitlink_blocks.
- R3-M1: AC clauses broader than named tests. Fix: §5 rebuilt as one-to-one AC→test table (new: test_stdlib_only_no_network, test_oversized_blob_blocks, test_shallow_clone_or_missing_base_fails_closed).

Audit trail kept honest: round-2 appendix rows B1–B4 re-annotated from FIXED to "partial → completed v0.4.0"; round-3 appendix added. CFADA round 4 (Codex) launched against head 1364d45. Loop continues to 0 blockers, then STOP for Michael's AuthorityDecision (§7: wiki-only, draft-PR-only, no merge). Blocker trajectory: r1=4, r2=4+1M, r3=6+1M — round 3 grew because the v0.3.0 repairs added attack surface; the class lesson (outcome lanes must be provably deny-by-default) held, the instances keep moving. Related markers: wiki-secret-scan-cfada-r2-repaired, wiki-secret-scan-tlc-checkpoint.

(2) The committed-tree scan is the §6 evidence AND caught that raw/ Open Brain exports ARE in the tree (5.7MB, 202 blobs).

[MARKER: wiki-secret-scan-cfar-r1r2-fixed · commit wiki@98306f5 · 2026-07-02] CFAR loop progress on transpara-ai/wiki PR #41 (https://github.com/transpara-ai/wiki/pull/41, draft, feat/wiki-secret-scan-hook). Author=Claude → reviewer=Codex (bare `codex exec review --base origin/main` per runbook; the cross-family-review-guard requires the command run bare, not compounded with other quoted commands — first attempt in a && chain was denied by the hook).

CFAR round 1 (head 0f47e6d): 2 findings, both real fail-open lanes, both FIXED @ 40fd50f:
- F1 (P2): future-dated reviewed_on let expires_on extend the 180-day validity window years past today → validator now rejects reviewed_on > today.
- F2 (P2): allowlist read from the WORKING TREE — Codex ran a live repro proving an UNSTAGED .secretsallow entry cleared a STAGED secret (commit would land without its review record). Fix: snapshot rule — --staged reads the INDEX copy (:0:compile/.secretsallow), --changed-against reads HEAD's, --tree reads <rev>'s; absent-from-snapshot = empty; git error = block. New named test test_allowlist_snapshot_matches_scan_mode; write_allowlist test helper now stages the file (review record travels with the commit).

CFAR round 2 (head 40fd50f): 2 findings, CI-trust class, both FIXED @ 98306f5:
- F3 (P1): CI executed the PR HEAD's scanner — a PR editing secret_scan.py could neuter the gate scanning itself. Fix: CI extracts the scanner from the TRUSTED base ref (git show "$BASE":compile/secret_scan.py → $RUNNER_TEMP/secret_scan_trusted.py) and runs that copy; bootstrap fallback to head copy ONLY when the base predates the scanner (i.e. the introducing PR). Residual (g) added honestly: ci.yml itself is PR-editable under the pull_request model — visible in review, not self-protectable without settings changes (out of scope).
- F4 (P2): scan step ran AFTER pip install/npm ci → untrusted install-time lifecycle code executed before the gate. Fix: step moved immediately after checkout/setup-python, before ALL installs (scanner is stdlib-only).

All fixes TDD (test first, RED verified, then implementation). Suite now 27 named tests, all green at 98306f5; wiring test hardened to assert trusted-copy extraction AND scan-before-install ordering. Design packet §3/§3.1.1/§5/§7 updated in the same commits so spec matches implementation. CFAR round 3 in flight at 98306f5. ## 2026-07-02 · ??

[MARKER hive-pr242-71594b2b 2026-07-02T18:05Z] Fixed flaky test TestPostEventIssueScanProgressDoesNotWaitForConfiguredRunner in transpara-ai/hive (branch feat/post-event-progress-test-deadline, commit 71594b2b1beac66b2fc8fd28ba994e6e8396eabc, PR #242). Root cause investigation, not a band-aid: the test guards the lock-stall fix from ed71a58 (configured issue-scan review runners used to run inside issueScanLifecycleMu, blocking post-event progress). It raced the post-event inline pass against a 200ms wall-clock deadline. An instrumented discriminator variant (15 runs on the loaded 4-core nucbuntu host, load avg ~6) showed the inline pass finishing ON ITS OWN in 208-589ms while the runner stayed blocked — coupling branch fired 0/15, so independence holds and the failure was pure scheduling noise + ~130ms of legitimate store scanning against a near-zero-margin budget. Fix: deadline 200ms → 10s with a comment recording the happens-before argument — release only closes after done, so a coupled implementation can never close done before ANY finite deadline; the timeout bounds 'blocked forever', it does not assert latency, so raising it loses zero detection power. Key debugging pattern worth reusing: when a 'must not block' test fails, distinguish coupled (done only after release) from slow-but-independent (done closes on its own past the deadline) by keeping the release gate open after the deadline miss and observing which channel closes first. Class sweep: all other sub-second time.After deadlines in hive tests (pkg/loop, pkg/membrane) are the inverse assert-nothing-arrives shape (timeout firing = pass) and cannot false-fail. Verification: target test 10/10 PASS on the same loaded host, full pkg/hive suite ok (76.7s), go vet clean, Codex cross-family review 0 blockers, gate posted success on exact head, PR #242 marked ready for Michael.

[MARKER: wiki-secret-scan-cfar-f10-f14 · commit wiki@ceb8487 · 2026-07-02] CFAR loop rounds 8-10 on transpara-ai/wiki PR #41 (secret-scan). Findings F10–F14, all fixed via TDD, suite now 32 named tests:

- F10 (P2, @be2970d): duplicate JSON keys inside one .secretsallow record — json.loads silently keeps the LAST value, so the parsed identity could differ from the raw reviewed record. Fix: object_pairs_hook raising on duplicates. LESSON: any reviewed-record format parsed by a lenient parser needs duplicate-member rejection.
- F11 (P3, @be2970d): date.fromisoformat accepts compact/week spellings (20260702, 2026-W27-4); documented grammar is exactly YYYY-MM-DD → explicit shape regex before parsing.
- F12 (P2, @addec28): oversized blobs were fully materialized BEFORE the size check — multi-GB accident would OOM the hook instead of cheaply blocking. Fix: cat-file -s decides; content only ever STREAMED (chunked sha256) to verify an existing blob_review. Test proves non-materialization by stubbing read_blob to raise.
- F13 (P2, @addec28): THE EXPIRY WEDGE — an expired entry in the BASE allowlist blocked every PR including the renewal PR itself (with 80 entries expiring 2026-12-29 this was a scheduled repo-wide deadlock). Fix: changed-against splits allowlist roles — clearance only from base's VALID entries; invalid base entries VOID with loud report (not fatal); head copy stays STRICT-validated (never used for clearance per F9). Net: expiry still forces renewal repo-wide (ordinary PRs inherit the expired entry in head → block) but the renewal PR — whose head is fixed — always passes. Wedge-free forcing function.
- F14 (P2, @ceb8487): secrets in the PATHNAME itself (cfg/sk-<token>/note.txt with clean content) passed both gates. Fix: the pathname is a scan unit. KEY DESIGN MOMENT: my first fix made path findings fingerprint-clearable — the test immediately exposed a SELF-REFERENTIAL REGRESS (the entry's canonical_path field embeds the secret-bearing path → .secretsallow itself flags → clearing that changes .secretsallow's blob → its own entry invalidates). Resolution: path findings are NON-CLEARABLE; remediation is a rename. Fail-safe cost asymmetry: wrongly-denied = a rename; wrongly-permitted = a committed secret. Verified zero existing tree paths trip any detector.

Design packet kept in sync every round (§3, §3.1, §3.1.1, §5). CI Build & Test green at each pushed head. CFAR round 11 in flight at ceb8487. Cumulative CFAR tally: 14 findings over 10 rounds, every one repaired at the head that followed. Related markers: wiki-secret-scan-cfar-r1r2-fixed, wiki-secret-scan-BUILT.

PROCESS LESSON (non-obvious): the reviewer ran `git checkout HEAD -- store.go` during its revert-check in the SAME worktree — any uncommitted edit there would be silently destroyed; likely how the store.go half of the shape fix vanished. Rule: commit everything before dispatching a reviewer into a shared worktree, and reviewers must restore via stash, not checkout. Also: tests that nil-normalize before DeepEqual (sortedCopy nil→[]) are structurally blind to wire-shape (null vs []) regressions — shape assertions must compare without normalization. [marker: eventgraph-839b16d0-2026-07-02T22:10:17+01:00] transpara-ai/eventgraph, branch feat/inmemory-paginate-cursor-index, commit 839b16d0924a7c5ea3333ff53aa597ca3255843a, PR #73 (draft, CFAR pending). Fixed quadratic pagination in InMemoryStore (go/pkg/store/memory.go): paginateReverse resolved cursors by linearly scanning the type/source/conversation index slice comparing event ID strings, making a K-page walk O(N*K). Root cause was found via pprof while benchmarking transpara-ai/work's frontier-based incremental fold (store_fold_cache.go ListSummariesCached) at 25k vs 50k events — cold fold scaled 2.28x instead of ~2x; the excess was this store scan, not the fold. Fix: resolve cursor via the pre-existing byID map (event ID → global position) + slices.BinarySearch over the ascending index slice (store is append-only so index slices are provably ascending — documented on the struct fields). No new state; in-memory analogue of pgstore's indexed id→seq lookup. Fail-closed semantics preserved and pinned by tests: malformed/unknown/case-variant/wrong-index cursors all still return InvalidCursorError (types.NewEventID lowercases, so an explicit id.Value() != cursor.Value() check stops case-variant cursors from silently starting to resolve — the subtle bug a naive fix would introduce). TDD: TestByTypeMultiPageWalkScalesLinearly written first, failed at 10.9x ratio on old code, passes at 3.4x after (threshold 8x, 2.5k vs 10k events). A/B benchmark 25k events full ByType walk: 127ms → 47ms. Gotcha learned: git stash is shared across worktrees of a repo — a `git stash pop` in a scratch worktree popped an unrelated parked entry (codex-stale-eventgraph-pr70-model-config-patch) causing conflicts; restored files from HEAD, stash entry preserved. Also: pre-existing staticcheck U1000 dead type at mysqlstore.go:743, spun off as a separate task chip.

TWO CFAR rounds run (Claude authored → Codex gpt-5.5 xhigh reviewed): round 1 at draft (0 blockers; Codex independently ran the timing regression test 20x + 3x under -race), round 2 forced fresh at the ready transition — learned/confirmed: eventgraph's "Seed external review status" job RESETS cross-family-adversarial-review to pending with "Ready-state exact-head cross-family review required" when a PR flips draft→ready, so the CFAR must be re-run and re-posted at the SAME head after gh pr ready, even with zero new commits. Both CFAR records posted as PR comments (4870530647, 4870568046). Residual risk recorded on the PR: the scaling regression test is timing-based; worst observed ratio across 25+ runs is 6.1x vs the 8.0x threshold (typical 3.4-4.4x); remedy if it ever flakes is widening the N spread, not loosening the threshold. Operational gotcha hit and worked around: the cross-family-review-guard hook blocks any Bash command whose text contains the codex review invocation string — posting a PR comment QUOTING the command tripped it; workaround is writing the comment body to a file with the Write tool and using gh pr comment --body-file. Scratch worktree removed; canonical clone repos/eventgraph back clean on main; merge remains Michael's decision.

## 2026-07-02 · ??

MARKER: work-cfar1-fixes-f7409c1 2026-07-02T23:59:00Z. Repo transpara-ai/work, branch feat/tasks-incremental-fold (worktree work-b3-tasks-fold), commit f7409c1 on top of 8b39d3d. Fixed both P2 defects from the codex cross-family review (CFAR round 1) of the fold cache, red/green proven each. CFAR-1: scratchRebuildAndServe (the fail-closed fallback) promoted the scratch fold UNCONDITIONALLY under the post-fold head — a write landing mid-foldFromScratch after its type was scanned appears in headAfter but not in the fold, so the stale fold got memoized under the new head and every subsequent same-head request memo-hit stale output until the next append. Fix mirrors rebuildOrIncrement's stable/provisional rule: read head before the fold, re-read after, promote only on equality; provisional folds served but never memoized. Deterministic test via a new one-shot fault-store ByType hook (armAfterByTypeOnce) armed on work.task.completed (scanned after work.task.created, never reached by the increment that aborts at assigned on the omitEventID frontier-miss fault) whose hook appends a task mid-scratch-fold; red showed the exact stale-memo symptom (task 3 missing from the NEXT call). CFAR-2: promote() called TimestampMS on a possibly-zero stableHead — a fold memoized against a GENUINELY empty store (Head none, the documented D2 zero-head case) holds the zero EventID, and types.EventID{}.TimestampMS() panics (slices "" [:12]); the first post-append /tasks request panicked. Fix: decide zero-head pairings before any TimestampMS call — held-zero vs real promotes (zero strictly older than any real head), real vs zero-candidate refuses fail-safe, zero-vs-zero already caught by the same-head replace branch. Class sweep confirmed this is the ONLY TimestampMS site in non-test code and promote() has exactly two callers. Non-obvious gotchas worth remembering: (1) setupStore bootstraps a genesis event, so the zero-head case is invisible to all existing tests — reproducing it needs a raw store.NewInMemoryStore with bootstrap performed AFTER the first fold; (2) singleflight re-panics fold panics into callers, so the zero-head bug takes down HTTP requests, not just a background goroutine; (3) the "stable/provisional" discipline must be applied at EVERY promote call site — the normal path had it, the fail-closed fallback didn't (fix-the-class lesson: when a rule guards one caller of a shared primitive, sweep all callers). Verified: build/vet clean, full go test ./... green (60.7s), -race FoldCache|ListSummariesCached|Promote green (290.4s). Nothing pushed.

## 2026-07-03 · ??

Fixed a fail-open ordering hole in the model catalog duplicate guard in transpara-ai/eventgraph (branch feat/catalog-two-pass-collision-guard, PR #76, commit a7199e6afc0a25220b55f066f6d6d359750a45fb, 2026-07-03T08:26:47+01:00). Root cause: NewCatalog in go/pkg/modelconfig/catalog.go populated the byID index incrementally in a single pass, so an EARLY entry's alias colliding with a LATER entry's ID passed the guard silently (the alias-vs-ID check only saw IDs indexed so far, and the ID check never consulted byAlias); Lookup then shadowed the alias because IDs resolve before aliases. Fix: two-pass validation — index all IDs first, then check every alias against the complete ID set — same maps and error messages, order-independent guard. Added TestNewCatalog_CollisionDomain pinning the whole collision input domain (id/id, alias/alias across entries both orders and within one entry, alias/id both orders, alias-equals-own-ID, valid catalog); the alias-before-colliding-ID case failed red before the fix, 8/8 green after. Full go test ./..., go vet, staticcheck all clean. Bug found during the B4 model-catalog review (feat/model-catalog-mode); pre-existing, not triggered by any current catalog, landed as its own one-concern PR. General lesson (same class as the hive#131 fail-safe spiral): a uniqueness guard built on incrementally-populated indexes is only closed over one ordering — cross-category checks (alias vs ID) must run against the complete set, and the test must cover every pair type in every entry order. Process note: the eventgraph "Seed external review status" CI job resets the cross-family-adversarial-review commit status to pending on the draft-to-ready transition ("Ready-state exact-head cross-family review required") — re-run the gate --post at the same head after gh pr ready and verify by status read-back. Codex reviewed the Claude-authored diff (bare codex exec review against origin/main): 0 blockers, verdict pass.

## 2026-07-03 · ??

[MARKER: work-server-unit-snap-scope-fix-2026-07-03T09:44Z] Fixed the work-server systemd user unit on nucbuntu (~/.config/systemd/user/work-server.service, host-level config — no repo change). Bug: ExecStart=/snap/bin/go run ./cmd/work-server made restarts unreliable — on `systemctl --user restart work-server` the go-run parent died but the compiled child (running from ~/.cache/go-build/...) kept port 8080, and the new instance crash-looped with "bind: address already in use" until the orphan was killed manually (bit us 2026-07-03 during the Mission Control 4-build deploy). Root cause: /snap/bin/go is a symlink to /usr/bin/snap, so the unit actually ran `snap run go`; snapd moves the whole process tree into its own transient scope (snap.go.go-<uuid>.scope), leaving work-server.service's cgroup EMPTY (Tasks: 0 in systemctl status). systemd's default control-group kill therefore had nothing to kill — it could only signal the MainPID (go run), and the child in the foreign snap scope survived holding the port. KillMode tweaks cannot fix this class of bug; the process must actually live in the unit's cgroup. Fix (site.service pattern): ExecStartPre=/snap/bin/go build -o /Transpara/transpara-ai/repos/work/work-server ./cmd/work-server, then ExecStart that binary directly — a plain ELF spawned by systemd stays in the service cgroup and dies with it. (ExecStartPre through the snap wrapper is fine: it's run-to-completion, systemd just waits for exit.) Kept EnvironmentFile=/home/transpara/.config/hive/hive.env and the /tmp/work-server.log StandardOutput/StandardError append redirects. The work repo's .gitignore already ignores /work-server so the built binary is invisible to git. Verified: two consecutive `systemctl --user restart work-server` runs — old MainPID reaped, port 8080 rebound by the new MainPID inside the service cgroup, /health returned {"status":"ok"} both times, NRestarts stayed 0, no stray work-server processes, no bind errors in the log. General lesson for nucbuntu: never ExecStart a snap-wrapped interpreter/launcher (`/snap/bin/*`) as a daemon in a systemd unit — snap's scope migration breaks systemd's process lifecycle management.

---

[OB-MARKER IADA-IAR-SKILL-DRAFT 2026-07-03T00:00Z-session-ace966c2] Design decision — drafted two new governance-gate skills (IADA = internal-adversarial-design-assessment, IAR = internal-adversarial-review) to sit alongside the existing CFADA/CFAR skills in transpara-ai/platform tools/transpara-governance-gates/skills/. Drafts currently live in scratchpad only (NOT committed) because Codex is still modifying the platform repo; deploy waits until it settles, off a fresh branch from the latest head. Base mirror head at draft time: platform HEAD 187698253739bacaad779d0c9727b798daf4a578 ("Harden design gate evidence flags", 2026-07-03).

WHAT WAS CHOSEN: skills lead with a POSITIVE result-standard contract (the canonical iada.result.md / iar.result.md artifact shape — assessor/assessed_at, scope audit, blocker checks, residual risks, explicit "ready for CFADA/CFAR: yes/no", and the "does not replace external CFADA/CFAR" boundary line) plus structural REQUIRED fields, and keep discipline lean. They explicitly SUBTRACT the gate machinery the cross-family skills carry: no commit-status posting, no cfada/cfar result schema, no post_commit_status helper — IADA/IAR produce durable supporting evidence and a self-directed PR-visible note, never a gate result.

WHAT WAS REJECTED: a prohibition-heavy discipline document. RED-phase baseline (two subagents inheriting the global CLAUDE.md, no skill text) showed discipline was ALREADY bulletproof — both refused to fail open, self-authorize, or self-post — so the real gap was WRONG-SHAPE OUTPUT, not weak discipline. Per superpowers writing-skills "match the form to the failure", wrong-shape → positive recipe, not prohibitions (which backfire under competing incentives).

REASONING/EVIDENCE: RED baselines caught all planted defects but emitted ad-hoc markdown with no canonical artifact, no explicit readiness verdict, no rerun-on-head-change. GREEN verification (same fixtures + skill text) produced the exact iada.result.md / iar.result.md shape, the explicit "Ready: No" verdict, residual risks with named owners, and every discipline refusal preserved — no loopholes, no regression, no REFACTOR round needed. Grounded against canonical doc dark-factory/v4.0/07-cfar-cfada-dev-arc-gate-standard-v4.0.md (v4.0.3) and real artifacts under docs/.adversarial-design/*-iada/ and docs/.adversarial-review/*-iar/. Tracked upstream by transpara-ai/platform#44 (full TLC/IADA/IAR/CFADA/CFAR package expansion). Repo=transpara-ai/platform, no branch yet.

[OB-MARKER TLC-12STEP-REFACTOR 2026-07-04T-session-a9ec9036] Michael restated TLC (Transpara Lifecycle for Code) as a canonical 12-step sequence (2026-07-04): 1 ingest work (auto or human) → 2 semver docs → 3 design → 4 IADA (iterate to 0 DESIGN blockers) → 5 CFADA (0 design blockers) → 6 Human Design Review (approve = pass; deny + comments = send back upstream) → 7 write code (0 REQUIREMENTS blockers) → 8 create draft PR → 9 IAR (0 CODE blockers) → 10 CFAR (0 code blockers) → 11 mark PR ready → 12 Human Review (approve = merge; deny + comments = send back upstream). Key refinements vs prior memory: the stage-6 human gate is named "Human Design Review" (the AuthorityRequest→External-Committee AuthorityDecision machinery formalizes it); BOTH human gates carry an explicit deny→upstream repair loop; blockers are TYPED per stage (design/requirements/code); draft PR creation (8) precedes IAR (9) — the IAR of record runs at the draft PR's exact head.

Actions taken: (a) updated auto-memory transpara-lifecycle-for-code-tlc.md with the 12-step numbering + renamed stage-6 gate; (b) refactored the Claude alt-draft IADA/IAR skills in /Transpara/transpara-ai/scratch/iada-iar-alt-drafts-claude/ — typed blockers, IAR moved to post-draft-PR of-record ordering, deny→upstream loops encoded in both, README updated with refactor note. (c) Checked Codex's transpara-lifecycle-for-code SKILL.md at platform#45 head 1876982: it ALREADY encodes the identical 12-step order, typed blockers, and deny loops — so stage order is NOT a CFAR finding against platform#45; the remaining substantive design question for that review is whether internal stages (IADA/IAR) should have result schemas (Codex added iada/iar-result.schema.json; Claude's alt drafts argue internal stages emit evidence, not gate results, so no schema). ## 2026-07-04 · ??

[OB-MARKER TLC-FACTORY-ORDERS-VERDICTS 2026-07-04T-session-a9ec9036-r2] Michael issued two standing TLC verdicts + restored one omitted stage (2026-07-04, follow strictly):

VERDICT 1 — semver is a birth-and-mutation rule, NOT a stage: every governed doc (Factory Order, design packet, …) carries doc_id/version/status frontmatter from creation and bumps on every material change, including deny-loop repairs. The old "semver docs" stage-2 slot is retired.

VERDICT 2 — the design-side truth object is the MARKDOWN PACKET AT EXACT GIT BLOB SHA, with semver as the human-readable label on top. Gate credit (IADA/CFADA/Human Design Review approval) binds to doc_id + version + blob SHA, never to a version string alone (mutable in place = fail-open). Precedent: docs#259 Decision 3 bound to packet blob e527f0e byte-identical. This is the design-side analog of CFAR's exact-head-SHA rule.

NEW STAGE — CRAFT FACTORY ORDERS (occupies stage 2, between ingest and design): turn partially-structured GitHub issues (channel B scrape) or unstructured human documents (channel A) into a verifiable requirements doc. TLC had accidentally omitted this. The FO completes the truth chain: raw intake (mutable) → Factory Order (immutable verifiable requirements) → design packet (immutable proposal, ACs trace to FO requirements) → code (reality). It fixes a latent hole: CFADA previously adjudicated "fidelity to intent" against mutable issues, which TLC itself rules out as evidence. It also gives step-7 "requirements blockers" a crisp meaning: trace chain FO requirement → AC(verification_method) → test → code; broken link = blocker; green ACs violating an FO requirement = design defect discovered late → upstream return.

Revised canonical 12 steps: 1 ingest → 2 craft Factory Order → 3 design → 4 IADA (0 design blockers) → 5 CFADA → 6 Human Design Review (deny+comments→upstream) → 7 code (0 requirements blockers) → 8 draft PR → 9 IAR (0 code blockers) → 10 CFAR → 11 mark ready → 12 Human Review (approve=merge).

SEQUENCING NOTE: accepted standard 07-cfar-cfada-dev-arc-gate-standard v4.0.3 and Codex's platform#45 skills still encode semver-as-stage and have NO Factory Order stage. Per TLC's own recursion these verdicts land via a docs standard bump (its own TLC arc — this conversation is that arc's channel-A ingest) BEFORE platform skills follow. NOT retroactive CFAR blockers against platform#45, which correctly matches the currently-accepted standard.

Files updated: auto-memory transpara-lifecycle-for-code-tlc.md + MEMORY.md index; Claude alt drafts in /Transpara/transpara-ai/scratch/iada-iar-alt-drafts-claude/ (packet blob-SHA binding now REQUIRED in both Result Standards, FO trace checks added to blocker hunts, stage listings corrected, README rev-2 note). Repo=transpara-ai (memory+scratch only; no git repo touched).

## 2026-07-07 · ??

[DIAG-capability-sync-28856505513 2026-07-07T09:55:00Z] Root cause of transpara-ai/platform "Capability Sync" GitHub Actions workflow failing on every scheduled run (runs #98–#109, Jun 26–Jul 7 2026, all ~10s failures): the workflow (.github/workflows/capability-sync.yml, daily cron 06:00 UTC) sets GH_TOKEN from secrets.CLAUDE_CODE, but that secret does not exist in the repo — the only repo Actions secret is OPENAI_API_KEY. GH_TOKEN resolves empty, so the first gh CLI call ("gh project item-list 37 --owner transpara") fails with "set the GH_TOKEN environment variable" and the job exits 1 before doing anything. What the task is: docs/_build/capability_sync.py scans merged PRs across transpara (company org, not transpara-ai) product repos (tview, tstore-interface, tgraph-api, tcalc, tsystem-api, tstudio-py, Excel-add-in, tai-gateway, tauth-scraper, transpara-py-sdk, tinstaller) for capability:X-NN labels from the last 48h, comments on linked issues, and conservatively upgrades capability status on GitHub Project #37 (owner transpara) — forward-only rank upgrades, frozen statuses (Shipped, Gap, Deferred) never auto-changed. Fix requires adding a CLAUDE_CODE secret containing a PAT with repo + project scopes on the transpara org (classic PAT needed for org-level Projects v2 access; github.token cannot reach another org's project). Diagnosed for Michael; no fix applied — assessment only.

PR-C (#61) = the design gap Path A exposed: quarantine_payload has NO runtime attestation by design, so a reviewed-false-positive doc could be COMMITTED (allowlist) but never REGISTERED (manifest audit gap). The principled lane: register's payload is a COMMITTED file → findings attest against the commit-time allowlist at the scanner's own identity tuple (rule_id, canonical_path, sha256(bytes), match_sha256, byte_offset). SIX Codex CFAR rounds hardened it: r1 fixture expiry time-bomb; r2 UTC-vs-local date skew; r3 P2 trust root = COMMITTED HEAD snapshot never the working tree (attack test: unstaged allowlist edit refuses); r4 P1 source_ref must exist at HEAD BYTE-EXACTLY (attack test: clearance-committed-ahead-of-file refuses — my own A→B pattern was the attack template!); r5 undecodable allowlist refuses through the controlled lane; ready-state: TOCTOU (HEAD resolved once, pinned commit backs both reads) + GIT_NO_LAZY_FETCH=1 on all attestation reads (air-gap fail-closed). 91 ops tests, verify exit 0 at every head.

BLOCKED-BY-CONCURRENCY (not failure): the final hermes register must run on the SERVING clone (the live service's root) — currently checked out on feat/pageindex-code-anchored-eval (Michael's concurrent TAI-RES-2026-007 arc, committing live: 18bb6dc 12:09, 1dec9f2 12:28 local) with my earlier restart having loaded THAT branch's pre-#61 code (hence the register 422 with the bare-quarantine message — diagnosis: serving clone diverged from origin/main, git pull 'Already up to date' because the BRANCH has no upstream). LESSONS: (1) content-addressed sha-suffix filenames are entropy-rule landmines — hex-free lowercase names are the law (the scanner's path findings are non-clearable BY DESIGN); (2) `git checkout -- <path>` restores from the INDEX — after a blocked commit, use git restore --source=HEAD --staged --worktree; (3) whole-file re-serialization of a security allowlist obscures the real delta — edit JSONL line-wise; (4) the serving clone is a SHARED mutable surface: always verify branch + HEAD before deploy actions, never assume main. ## 2026-07-07 · ??

MARKER: TAI-RES-2026-007-pageindex-eef5df6 (2026-07-07). Repo transpara-ai/wiki, branch feat/pageindex-code-anchored-eval, PR #62 (READY, cross-family status success at head eef5df64782d685c89ce94ee5124cd6cc6bb2f6f; Michael merges).

What: re-evaluated PageIndex (VectifyAI/PageIndex @ f413c66, 2026-07-03) the same way MemPalace was (TAI-RES-2026-004) — a code-anchored read of the real repo — and upgraded wiki/pageindex.md from an indexed-only stub to a code-anchored assessment, surfacing findings into the contribution-box (renders in the 2nd-paragraph slot). New eval: raw/civilization/external-landscape/tai-res-2026-007-pageindex-evaluation.md.

Key code-anchored findings (non-obvious):
- For a PDF (PageIndex's default + benchmarked path) the tree index is a probabilistic LLM artifact: every node/title/page-map/summary is a gpt-4o output (page_index.py), self-graded by an LLM accuracy check at a hard-coded 0.6 threshold with a fallback cascade (verify_toc/meta_processor). Building a PDF index REQUIRES an external LLM API (litellm->OpenAI) — inverse of MemPalace's local-first posture; collides with air-gap + Base Slice 0.
- The Markdown path is the deterministic exception: md_to_tree parses # headers with a regex + level stack (page_index_md.py:32/190), no LLM for structure (LLM only for optional summaries). Do NOT over-generalize the LLM-artifact claim to Markdown (a CFAR R2 fix).
- The OSS library ships only 3 dumb accessor tools (retrieve.py); the "reasoning retrieval / AlphaGo tree search" is a caller's OpenAI-Agents-SDK loop, not the library (no search algorithm).
- Two PageIndexes: MIT OSS lib (no git tags/releases) vs cloud product; `pip install pageindex` is the CLOUD SDK (BASE_URL api.pageindex.ai), not the indexer.
- 98.7% FinanceBench is Mafin 2.5's (a system powered by PageIndex), self-reported by VectifyAI, no independent reproduction.
- CodeQL scans only Actions YAML (build-mode none), NOT the Python — security-tooling gap.

Doctrine + §4.4 determination: PageIndex maps to the accepted-v3.9 DocumentEvidenceRetrieval node schema (02:331) -> KnowledgeReference/source_refs; no ADR exists; none created now; PATTERN-ONLY; gated behind Base Slice 0; never truth/cert/authority (Decision 15). Corrected the wiki's implication that PageIndex isn't in accepted doctrine (it IS named in v3.9 06:178 and 09:252). Two doctrine gaps surfaced: v4.0 didn't restate DocumentEvidenceRetriever; no PageIndex row in the v3.9.1 crosswalk.

Reusable process notes:
- Session-authored evals -> raw/civilization/external-landscape/ (lowercase filename), NOT raw/inbox (browser-ingest only). Audit-pin the eval's sha256 in the citing article's raw_documents comment (PROVENANCE convention; owainlewis sibling pattern).
- The wiki contribution-box renders from civilization_contribution frontmatter for tier:investigation pages, spliced right after paragraph 1 (build_site.py:2170 lead_intro+contribution+lead_tail) = the "2nd paragraph" slot.
- YAML frontmatter: avoid ': ' (colon-space) inside unquoted confidence values — strict YAML breaks, but build_site.py's parser is lenient and hides it.
- CFAR mechanics: Claude authored -> Codex reviewed (codex exec review --base origin/main, bare). origin/main advanced mid-review (PR #61 merged) so I rebased onto current main to keep --base origin/main scoped to my 2 files, and ran the review in a clean detached git worktree to avoid the shared repo's unrelated dirty working tree. 4 rounds to 0 blockers; gate status posted via the gate tool and verified by commit-status read-back; PR marked ready.

[MARKER: wiki-nucbuntu-reboot-autorecovery-20260708T1213WEST · observed 2026-07-09 during session resume state-check]

OPERATIONAL EVENT (verified): host nucbuntu — the box running the transpara-ai/wiki (Civilization knowledge wiki) serving clone at /Transpara/transpara-ai/repos/wiki and its systemd USER service transpara-ai-civilization-wiki.service — REBOOTED on 2026-07-08 at ~12:13 WEST (approx 11:13Z), roughly 6 minutes AFTER the wiki-CHECKPOINT-20260708T1108Z checkpoint (2026-07-08T11:08Z). The wiki service AUTO-RECOVERED at boot with zero operator action.

EVIDENCE: `who -b` -> system boot 2026-07-08 12:13; `uptime -s` -> 2026-07-08 12:14:47 (derived, less precise than who -b); systemd ExecMainStartTimestamp -> Wed 2026-07-08 12:14:05 WEST; service MainPID changed 1415448 (the checkpoint's PID, from the 2026-07-08 ~10:49Z deploy restart) -> 1183 (a low post-boot PID — the tell that distinguished a reboot from a mere systemctl restart). Uptime at observation ~15h34m (=> now ~2026-07-09 03:48 WEST).

POST-REBOOT HEALTH (verified read-only 2026-07-09): ActiveState=active; :8787 all pages HTTP 200; serving clone git-clean on main @ 2c9e672 (Merge PR #68), `git status --porcelain` empty; manifest.d = 8 shards INCLUDING the #68-corrected new-named shards 1185147b38da / e1de4dd84243, with the old-named edd20ac8fb79 / f27d9ad20873 correctly ABSENT. Nothing lost, nothing to fix.

WHY IT WAS A NON-EVENT (design lesson): (1) all runtime state was durably COMMITTED via PR #68 BEFORE the reboot — the serving clone was clean-on-main, not a dirty working tree; had nucbuntu gone down during the earlier 2026-07-08 "soft deploy" window (24 uncommitted runtime-state files, durable only in the working tree at that time), recovery would have been git-history-only = much worse. (2) content-addressed shards (filename == sha256(row)[:12]) self-verify integrity with no separate checksum ledger to desync. (3) the systemd USER service auto-starts at boot — this reboot is real-world confirmation the install/enable is correct and survives reboots (notable given the nucbuntu snap-go daemon gotcha: this unit ExecStarts a real interpreter/path, not /snap/bin/*, so it restarts cleanly).

DISPOSITION: no wiki work performed; this is a read-only operational observation captured at Michael's request during session resume. No production EventGraph write, RuntimeBroker/runtime execution, deploy, restart, private fetch, protected settings change, Test 001 GREEN, production go-live, value allocation, or autonomy increase occurred. Did NOT use --admin. Updated branch locally (git merge origin/main, was 28 behind, my 2 files untouched, mergeable=MERGEABLE) → new head → re-ran full codex CFAR. The update surfaced 2 real provenance nits: r8 (PageIndex-007 merged to main in the interim, so my r5 'in-flight/not-on-origin-main' note went stale → dropped the volatile status, 007 now a normal companion) and r9 ('advisory-memory hygiene' paired with v4.0 doc 03, but that phrase is in the v4.0 implementation epics; doc 03 says 'memory and knowledge are advisory only' → cited doc 03's actual rule). r10 clean at head 45c7021. TOTALS: 10 codex review rounds (r1-r10), ~13 findings, ZERO blockers ever, all valid + fixed. KEY LESSON: after a branch-update-for-BEHIND you MUST re-run the exact-head CFAR (the update can introduce real staleness — e.g. a concurrent PR merging changes what 'in-flight' means); point-in-time status claims (PR in-flight, doc line numbers) are fragile and should be avoided or made robust. To land a merge against fast-moving main: keep local origin/main = merge base during re-review (don't fetch mid-review or the diff gets noisy), then check remote main hasn't advanced before investing in the review.

ALL findings were EVIDENCE-ACCURACY corrections (verdict + §4.4 determination never in question), each folded into a v1.0.0->v1.0.1 bump + revision row + content-hash cascade to the article's 2 sha256 refs (session-placed eval, NOT manifest-registered, so freely editable — unlike #50/#52 ledger docs): r1 'every source file' copyright->'most source files'; r2 callout 'throughout'->'most' + companion TAI-RES-2026-008 flagged 'missing' (REJECTED-with-evidence: OB1 raw doc + wiki/ob1.md ARE on origin/main); ready-r1 Go engine 'defaults to remote OPA/Cedar HTTP'->corrected (it's FAIL-CLOSED, Deny default policy.go:119-120, opt-in backends) + supply-chain-check.yml 'fails PRs'->'partial' (scans a non-existent root packages/ dir, inert); ready-r2 'all eight README adapters'->scoped (README 'Works With Your Stack' lists 12 named + '20+ more') + workflow count 35->34.

KEY LEARNINGS: (1) A dense code-anchored eval (~235 lines, ~40 file:line claims) has a long TAIL of evidence-precision nits Codex surfaces incrementally (~2/round, converging like #64's 7 rounds). PROACTIVE convergence = clone the fork at the pin and audit ALL exact numeric claims at once (verified 2608 python files, 128 agent-os/src copyright files, 7 fuzz harnesses, ~18 subprojects, 1568/1651=95% copyright coverage — all accurate) -> the next Codex round came back CLEAN. Don't just react round-by-round on a claim-heavy doc. (2) Codex CAN false-positive (companion-008 'not on main' when it IS) — reject-with-evidence via git ls-tree, don't blind-implement (receiving-review discipline; don't delete a valid reference to appease a wrong finding). (3) AGT internal inconsistency the review surfaced: Python PolicyEvaluator is fail-OPEN (default ALLOW, evaluator.py:220) but the Go PolicyEngine is fail-CLOSED (default Deny, policy.go:83,119-120) — noted in §2.8. (4) GATE MECHANICS at wiki: draft->ready did NOT re-pend cross-family status this time (stayed success at unchanged head c5f1ce9), differing from the wiki-CHECKPOINT '#26' note that draft->ready always re-seeds pending; what reliably re-pends is a HEAD CHANGE (each repair push seeds it pending), so re-run Codex + re-post gate at each new head; reviewed_sha must == live head or gate fails stale-SHA. (5) origin/main moved 2+ times during the work; left the branch BEHIND rather than chase (re-rebasing changes the head and invalidates the clean review). (6) cross-family-review-guard.sh blocks QUOTED echoes of the codex command in a Bash line — run it bare, redirect to a log, no surrounding echo strings. Repo transpara-ai/wiki. Related: wiki-CHECKPOINT-20260708T1108Z, wiki-nucbuntu-reboot-autorecovery-20260708T1213WEST.

## 2026-07-09 · ??

[MARKER: wiki-pr70-gate-reclobber-restored-20260709T0624Z · 2026-07-09T06:24Z] transpara-ai/wiki PR #70 (Investigation Topic Standard design packet; head 902e7ab64cbbb04209f8163bb2216cec92cfabdc; branch feat/investigation-standard-design) — on session resume the cross-family-adversarial-review commit STATUS was found live-PENDING, contradicting the 05:40Z handoff checkpoint [[wiki-CHECKPOINT-20260709T0540Z]] which claimed it success + read-back-verified.

ROOT CAUSE (forensic; evidence = status history + check-run timings): a DELAYED "Seed external review status" run clobbered the gate. Timeline at head 902e7ab: 05:32:06 gate posted success (draft CFAR); 05:32:54 Michael marked ready_for_review; 05:34:53 gate re-posted success (ready CFAR); then the ready_for_review event triggered a SECOND seed workflow (Cross-Family Review Status, event pull_request_target) that STARTED 05:37:59 and wrote status=pending at 05:38:03 — ~5 min AFTER the event and ~2 min BEFORE the 05:40 checkpoint. The prior session's status read-back saw success at 05:34:53 but the delayed seed re-pended AFTER that read, so the checkpoint's "success, verified" was STALE. TOCTOU fail-open: the read-back and the clobbering seed raced, the read won, the handoff reported a false green.

ARCHITECTURAL GAP (wiki CI): the seed workflow fires DELAYED (~5 min) on ready_for_review and re-seeds cross-family-adversarial-review=pending, which can clobber a gate success that cross_family_review_gate.py --post wrote in the interim. So "gh pr ready THEN post the gate" is racy — the seed can land after both. A point-in-time status read-back is NOT durable proof while a seed is still queued.

RESOLUTION (Michael chose "restore green now" via AskUserQuestion): re-ran Codex CFAR at the UNCHANGED head 902e7ab (codex exec review --base origin/main, BARE, from worktree /Transpara/transpara-ai/worktrees/wiki-investigation-standard) = PASS, 0 blockers, exactly 1 P2 = the already-adjudicated named residual C34 (§2.2 raw-ingested Topic-Details classifier stated as raw/inbox/ excludes TAI-RES docs relocated to raw/civilization/external-landscape/; disposition CARRIED non-blocking, pinned by Topic-Details tests at Phase-1 impl/IAR; packet row C34 + residual-risks a). Then posted fresh CFAR evidence comment issuecomment-4922170951 via gh pr comment --body-file (NOT inline — guard hook); gate dry-run passed:true -> --post --target-url <that comment> -> INDEPENDENT read-back = combined status success, cross-family=success, Build&Test success, AND `gh run list` showed NO in-flight runs (nothing queued to re-clobber; durable because ready_for_review already fired and no head change/toggle since).

END STATE: PR #70 OPEN, READY, mergeable MERGEABLE, mergeStateStatus BEHIND (GitHub compare: 17 ahead / 18 behind main@30deca6; the handoff's "11 behind" was imprecise — main unmoved). Gate genuinely green. Only remaining pre-merge factor is BEHIND -> admin-merge (checks-green-but-BEHIND, #56/#68 pattern) or branch-update, Michael's call at Human Design Review (TLC stage 6). Merge stays Michael's. NO code written (no code before HDR approval).

LESSON: after `gh pr ready` on wiki, the delayed seed WILL re-pend the cross-family status ~5 min later; the durable fix is to post/verify the gate AFTER the seed has drained AND pair the status read-back with a concurrent `gh run list --jq 'select(.status!="completed")'` in-flight check (empty [] = durable). A bare status read is fail-open if a seed is queued. Repo transpara-ai/wiki. Related: [[wiki-CHECKPOINT-20260709T0540Z]], [[wiki-investigation-standard-CFADA-PASS-PR70]], [[cfar-comment-guard-hook-workaround]].

## 2026-07-09 · ??

[MARKER: wiki-branch-cleanup-20260709T0640Z · 2026-07-09] transpara-ai/wiki branch/worktree hygiene sweep on Michael's "clean it up" (he separately enabled delete_branch_on_merge for future PRs). BEFORE: 19 remote branches (18 non-main), 6 worktrees, 21 stale local origin/* refs. AFTER: 4 remote (main; #70 feat/investigation-standard-design; #71 feat/wiki-secretsallow-sakana-repin; feat/wiki-nav-single-entry-remove-toc = empty scratch at main, staged for the investigation-standard Phase-1 nav work), 4 worktrees, 0 stale refs. Serving clone /Transpara/transpara-ai/repos/wiki LEFT UNTOUCHED (clean on main @ 30deca6) — all ops ran from worktrees.

DID: deleted 15 merged remote branches (each guarded by a live `gh api repos/transpara-ai/wiki/compare/main...<branch> ahead_by==0` check; fail-closed skip otherwise — 0 skipped); removed 2 merged-tip worktrees (wiki-tai-res-008-ob1 = #64, and wiki-r2 = #68 after the finding below); `git remote prune origin` from a worktree cleared 21 stale refs (15 just-deleted + 6 that were deleted-on-GitHub-but-never-pruned-locally, so `git branch -r` had been over-reporting). ROOT CAUSE of accumulation: delete_branch_on_merge was false + TLC mints a feat/ or codex/ branch per PR + inconsistent manual post-merge deletion (everything <=#32 had been cleaned; #33+ mostly not).

NON-OBVIOUS LEARNING 1 — a STALE WORKTREE can STRAND an unmerged authored commit. wiki-r2 (feat/runtime-state-20260707) was labeled "stale/merged #68" in prior notes, but its HEAD cdcfe2d (Michael-authored 2026-07-07 runtime state, NEVER pushed) was NOT an ancestor of main (`git merge-base --is-ancestor HEAD origin/main` exit 1). PR #68 merged the REMOTE tip df02c96; cdcfe2d was 1 local commit beyond it. The fail-safe gate caught it: inspected before deleting, refused to auto-drop authored-work-not-in-main, surfaced the contradiction, got explicit human OK (AskUserQuestion → "Drop it") before removing. LESSON: before `git worktree remove`, run `merge-base --is-ancestor HEAD origin/main`; an "ahead N of the pushed tip" status = unpushed local commits that die with the worktree.

NON-OBVIOUS LEARNING 2 — CONTENT-ADDRESSED manifest shards make SUPERSESSION look like DELETION. wiki manifest.d shard filenames embed sha256(content)[:12] (e.g. `…092837…-edd20ac8fb79.jsonl`). When #68 did the owner-instructed hex-free source-file renames, each affected shard's CONTENT changed (it stores the renamed `source_path`), so it got a NEW hash/filename (`…092837…-1185147b38da.jsonl`) — SAME timestamp prefix, SAME operation, new address. So cdcfe2d's 2 "absent-from-main" shards were just the pre-rename twins; matching on the TIMESTAMP prefix (not the hash) located their corrected forms in main. Proved cdcfe2d fully superseded (15/17 added files byte-present in main; the 2 absent = renamed twins present under corrected names; 6/7 modified files byte-identical, only PROVENANCE.md newer in main) → dropped, nothing lost. LESSON: when auditing a content-addressed store, match on the stable key (timestamp), not the content hash, or renames read as deletions. Repo transpara-ai/wiki. Related: [[wiki-clone-is-live-ingest-service-statedir]], [[tai-res-eval-placement-and-naming]], [[wiki-pr70-gate-reclobber-restored-20260709T0624Z]].
