Remote 15 -> 1 (just main): deleted all 14 non-main branches, each guarded by a live `gh api repos/transpara-ai/operation/compare/main...<b> ahead_by==0` check (0 skipped); deletes STUCK (no re-push, so it wasn't an active re-push loop). All 14 mapped to MERGED PRs (#37,#40,#42,#47,#48,#50,#51,#54,#55,#56,#58,#60,#61,#62; note #36 was CLOSED-unmerged on the reused runbook branch, #37 merged it).

KEY DIFFERENCE FROM WIKI: operation ALREADY had delete_branch_on_merge=TRUE (wiki's was false), so the 14 were a PRE-SETTING BACKLOG, not an ongoing leak — cleared once, stays clean, no checkbox needed. Also operation main is NOT branch-protected (wiki's IS).

LOCAL SIDE HELD (deliberately not touched) — the operation clone is an ACTIVE CODEX WORKSPACE, not a passive mirror like wiki's serving clone. /Transpara/transpara-ai/repos/operation is checked out on a FEATURE branch (codex/operation-59-source-route-posture, merged #60), local main BEHIND 34, with 2 satellite worktrees (operation-226-eventgraph-authority = merged #62 @ 9d99acc; operation-226-proposal-authority = merged #61 @ 1b06968) + .adversarial-review/ CFAR artifacts, mtimes as recent as 2026-07-09 06:42. Fail-safe inspection: ALL THREE checkouts CLEAN, HEAD is-ancestor-of-origin/main (exit 0 = merged), ZERO unpushed commits => NO data at risk (no stranded cdcfe2d-style work). The ONLY reason to hold is workspace-ownership/active-use: it's codex's live working clone, and removing its worktrees/branches has zero shared-repo benefit (remote already clean) with nonzero risk of disrupting an active codex session. Recommended leaving it to codex; offered Michael a full-parity local tidy (prune 14 stale refs + remove 2 merged worktrees + delete 7 merged local branches) on request.

LESSON: before replicating a cleanup across repos, RE-RUN the analysis — repos differ. wiki = delete_branch_on_merge false + passive-on-main serving clone => full remote+local sweep was right. operation = delete_branch_on_merge true (backlog only) + active-codex-workspace clone => remote-only sweep, HOLD local. Treat /Transpara/transpara-ai/repos/operation like a live workspace (analogous caution to [[wiki-clone-is-live-ingest-service-statedir]]): remote prune is safe/shared+reversible; local surgery needs a human nod. Repo transpara-ai/operation. Related: [[wiki-branch-cleanup-20260709T0640Z]].

The "Cross-Family Review Status" seed workflow did an UNCONDITIONAL `POST state=pending` on pull_request_target events; a run delayed by Actions queue latency could land after the reviewer re-posted the ready-state gate success and clobber it -> pending (false-green on PR #70). Fix authored by Claude, three draft PRs (all Claude-authored -> Codex CFAR), all off origin/main, do NOT merge (Michael's call):

1. transpara-ai/wiki branch feat/cross-family-seed-durability, commit 940eb4a. Replaces the unconditional POST with a tested fail-safe kernel `decide(current_state, current_updated_at, event_time)` in compile/seed_cross_family_status.py: PRESERVE a terminal status ONLY when provably newer than the triggering event (github.event.pull_request.updated_at); re-pend on every other input (none/pending/stale/equal/missing/malformed-timestamp/unknown-state/unreadable-read sentinel). 14 full-domain stdlib tests wired into npm run test:py. Workflow now checks out the BASE branch (ref: pull_request.base.ref, persist-credentials:false, contents:read added) and runs the trusted base copy — never PR-head code (pull_request_target safety preserved).

2. transpara-ai/docs branch feat/cfar-gate-durability-check, commit 6e6d90e. Defense-in-depth (option c) in tools/cross-family-review-gate/cross_family_review_gate.py: pure fail-closed is_durably_green(context_state, inflight_seed_runs) + a --check-durable mode (durable ONLY if status success AND zero in-flight seed runs; the point-in-time read-back alone is not proof). 6 new unittests. Also WIRED the gate tool's previously-unrun test suite into npm run verify (was missing) and added the missing __pycache__ .gitignore. README documents the paired read-back + in-flight verification step.

3. transpara-ai/docs branch feat/docs-cross-family-seed-durability, commit 87b9373. FIX-THE-CLASS: the docs seed workflow was byte-identical to wiki's (same bug). Ported the wiki fix to tools/cross-family-review-status/ (seed_cross_family_status.py + 14 unittests wired into verify + .gitignore + README + workflow rewrite).

Pre-flight (read-only, real GitHub data) confirmed the I/O wrappers: wiki current_context_status reads PR#70 head 902e7ab as ('success','2026-07-09T06:24:28Z'); docs fetch_inflight_seed_runs = 0 in flight; fetch_context_status = success. Only the runner's scoped-token permission (contents:read + statuses:write reading the combined /commits/{sha}/status endpoint) is unverifiable locally — CI confirms it. NEXT: create 3 draft PRs, IAR each, Codex CFAR (codex exec review --base origin/main, bare) to zero blockers, gate --post + durable read-back, gh pr ready; Michael merges. ## 2026-07-09 · ??

OPERATIONAL EVENT [marker: OPS-2026-07-09T1049WEST-viz-backend-crashloop] — On nucbuntu, the entire Transpara dark-factory Visualization Surface backend has been DOWN / crash-looping for ~3 days. Verified 2026-07-09 ~10:49 WEST by direct probing (not docs), during a "state of the Visualization Surface" review.

Symptom: three systemd --user services are all in "activating (auto-restart)" (a crash loop): work-server.service (serves :8080 /telemetry/* — Mission Control + Observatory feeder), site.service (binds :80, serves /ops/observatory + the whole /ops console + public site), hive-ops-api.service (serves :8085 /api/hive/operator-projection — Observatory authority/lifecycle/civ-assembly feeder). NRestarts ≈ work-server 7,693; hive-ops-api 15,507; site 15,495. curl http://localhost:8080/telemetry/status → HTTP 000 (connection refused). Nothing listening on :80 or :8080.

ROOT CAUSE (single): Postgres is down. Container hive-postgres-1 Exited (0) ~3 days ago (~2026-07-06) and was not restarted (no restart policy; box rebooted 2026-07-09 04:13 and the container did not come back). 127.0.0.1:5432 confirmed CLOSED via /dev/tcp probe. All three Go services dial :5432 at startup and exit 1:
- site.service journal: "ping db: dial tcp 127.0.0.1:5432: connect: connection refused" (DATABASE_URL=postgres://hive:hive@localhost:5432/site).
- hive-ops-api.service journal: "open eventgraph store: store unavailable: schema: failed to connect ... database=hive ... 127.0.0.1:5432: connect: connection refused".
- work-server.service: exits status=1 on every start (same 5432 dependency; telemetry tables live in hive-postgres). Its own error line wasn't separately captured but :5432 is confirmed closed and it shares the dependency — same root cause, high confidence.
site-postgres-1 container also Exited (255) ~5 days ago but maps host :5433 and is NOT referenced by current env (services all use :5432) — appears legacy/unused.

Code is healthy: site binary loads all content ("loaded 45 blog posts", "14 layers, 201 primitives, 28 agent primitives", "13 grammars + base grammar + cognitive grammar + code graph") and only dies on the DB ping. Pure data-layer outage, not a code regression. Classic "shipped ≠ running."

FIX: start hive-postgres-1 (docker start hive-postgres-1, or docker compose up -d postgres from the compose dir), confirm :5432 healthy and that databases "hive" and "site" exist; the three systemd services self-heal on their next ~10s restart tick. Then re-probe http://localhost:8080/telemetry/status and http://nucbuntu/ops/observatory. The hive runtime (cmd/hive agents) is separately NOT running — needed only to GENERATE fresh telemetry, not to SERVE existing dashboards. Do NOT touch container upstream-fork-sync-local-app-1 (upstream, unrelated). Repo/host: transpara-ai stack on nucbuntu.

CFAR took **17 ROUNDS** to reach 0 blockers — a claim-dense operational runbook; Codex ran commands (e.g. `ingest`, `council --catalog-reload-interval`) to PROVE failures. ~35 findings total, ALL accepted-and-repaired except ONE rejected-with-evidence: the ops-api catalog resolves to catalog-mixed.yaml via `systemctl --user show hive-ops-api -p Environment` (systemd last-wins), NOT catalog-codex.yaml — Codex misread the earlier Environment= line. Zero recurrences. The oscillation source was the manual-go-run-runtime restart handling; it converged once restart was made STOP-ONLY (print the running command, tell operator to re-run) per Codex's own recommendation — auto-relaunching a fixed `civilization daemon` was wrong (switched verb/governance). KEY LESSONS: (1) the marketplace-loaded skill was the ORIGINAL, not the user's modified tooling — always diff loaded-copy vs first-party repo source. (2) For claim-dense operational runbooks expect MANY CFAR rounds; "clever" auto-recovery logic generates findings — prefer simple stop + "re-run your exact command". DISCOVERY marker 20260710T0310Z-site-postgres-dead-rootcause: Root-caused why site-postgres-1 on nucbuntu shows "Exited (255) 5 days ago". (1) Immediate cause: the Jul 04 2026 06:06 WEST host reboot (last reboot shows boots Jul 04 06:06, Jul 04 09:32, Jul 08 12:13) — exit 255 with FinishedAt exactly equal to dockerd restore time is the ungraceful-daemon-stop signature; OOMKilled=false, logs clean. (2) Why it stayed dead: repos/site docker-compose.yml has no restart: policy (RestartPolicy=no) and no systemd wrapper starts the site compose stack, so it survived none of the three reboots. (3) Why nobody noticed: production site.service does NOT use it — DATABASE_URL=postgres://hive:hive@localhost:5432/site (the hive-postgres container, unit unchanged since Jun 22); site-postgres-1 (host :5433, anonymous volume, db/user 'site') is only the dev/test compose DB (its last traffic = test fixtures run_existing/run_global duplicate-key errors). (4) BIGGER adjacent finding: hive-postgres's volume hive_pgdata was created fresh 2026-07-04 11:27 — the compose project rename lovyou-ai-hive→hive changed the derived volume name, so the stack silently started on an EMPTY volume; the old lovyou-ai-hive_pgdata volume (created 2026-04-06) still exists orphaned and holds ALL pre-Jul-04 data: the old hive event chain AND the production site db (users/ops). Current site db in hive-postgres was auto-recreated ~Jul 09 18:34 WEST (site.service logged 'database site does not exist' 3D000 until then); it now has only 2 users / 7 ops rows, all dated Jul 09+. Any pre-Jul-04 production site data is recoverable from lovyou-ai-hive_pgdata. (5) Class problem (fail-safe): NO postgres container on this host has restart:unless-stopped — every reboot silently kills the DBs while the Go services keep serving HTTP 200, masking the failure. No fix applied yet — reported to Michael for decision (start site-postgres? add restart policies via PR? recover/retire old volume?). Host nucbuntu, repos transpara-ai/site + transpara-ai/hive.

## 2026-07-10 · ??

ARCH-FINDING marker 2026-07-10T11:45Z-ccd-persession-skill-snapshots — Non-obvious ccd/Cowork runtime behavior discovered on nucbuntu while verifying the hive-lifecycle cloud-skill deletion. The ccd remote runtime materializes a SEPARATE per-session (per-materialization) SNAPSHOT of each plugin bundle into a hash-named dir under ~/.claude/remote/plugins/. There are 614 such dirs; 278 of them are copies of the SAME 'anthropic-skills' bundle (confirmed via each dir's .claude-plugin/plugin.json name == 'anthropic-skills'), each carrying whatever hive-lifecycle existed at that snapshot's creation. Live ccd-cli processes are launched with explicit --plugin-dir <hash> flags naming a session-specific subset; different running sessions reference DIFFERENT anthropic-skills snapshots (e.g. this session -> cc1b0a9fcaab3079; other running sessions -> 3d964889069cc41a and 8e2eee8bd48f7514, both still listing the stale hive-lifecycle). IMPLICATIONS for deleting a cloud user skill: (1) The authoritative fix is deleting it at the cloud source (claude.ai) — Michael did this for skill_013o5cwooNphyEJTf1M5gmTm. (2) Local snapshots do NOT update instantly: the anthropic-skills manifest.json lastUpdated on this machine decoded to 2026-07-10 10:57 UTC, PREDATING the deletion, so a ccd bundle re-sync is still pending. (3) Existing snapshots (278) are stale cache; they self-heal only when ccd re-syncs the bundle from cloud (new content -> new bundle hash -> new sessions materialize without the skill). (4) Editing/removing the skill from a running session's snapshot does NOT unload it from that session's memory (plugins are read at process start). ACTION TAKEN this session: surgically removed hive-lifecycle from THIS session's snapshot cc1b0a9fcaab3079 (backed up its manifest to manifest.json.bak-hive-lifecycle-20260710T113923Z, python-filtered the manifest to preserve the other 8 skills, rm -rf the skill subdir; verified). Did NOT mass-purge the other 277 snapshots — they are harness-managed cache, some tied to running/paused-resumable sessions (--resume 362ad081, e47872bb), and they self-heal; mass surgery is high-blast-radius for self-healing downstream cache. DURABLE GUARANTEES now in place: cloud source deleted + personal global skill at ~/.claude/skills/hive-lifecycle/SKILL.md (new content, sha 503c7b34...). Host: nucbuntu.

## 2026-07-11 · ??

[hive c765d52 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r10] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=c765d52 — CFAR round-10 repairs (Codex reviewer, 2 P1s accepted; FO v0.12.0 R7 x-y): (1) SHELL GOTCHA worth remembering permanently: `names=$(tr '\0' '\n' </proc/$pid/environ 2>/dev/null | cut -d= -f1)` does NOT fail when the environ read fails — a pipeline's exit status is the LAST command's (cut, exit 0) unless pipefail is set, so a mid-restart read failure produced empty output → grep -cx printed 0 → misread as read-only while a writer-mode replacement process could be running. My round-9 reasoning ('redirect failure fails the substitution') was WRONG for redirects inside a pipeline stage. Fix pattern: capture the read FIRST as its own command — raw=$(cat /proc/$pid/environ 2>/dev/null) && [ -n \"$raw\" ] — then pipe the captured value. (2) The round-9 hive.service caution pointed at a running-process check that cannot work on a STOPPED unit (no MainPID) and named the wrong unit/var. Replaced with a real pre-start preflight in both dialects: names-only sweep of unit Environment= lines (systemctl --user cat), each EnvironmentFile (readable or block), and the user-manager environment (show-environment); any hit or unreadable source blocks start; plus a user-confirmed UnsetEnvironment=LOVYOU_API_KEY drop-in for local-only runtime and post-start /proc verification. Round 11 running at head c765d52687da6d496ea2d9cb5e2061d8f28a5b1d.

## 2026-07-11 · ??

[hive 26ae0e8 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r11] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=26ae0e8 — CFAR round-11 repairs (Codex reviewer, 3 findings; FO v0.13.0 R7 z-ab): (1) P1 CRITICAL SHELL GOTCHA, the inverse of round 10: `raw=$(cat /proc/pid/environ)` STRIPS NUL BYTES in bash command substitution, concatenating every env assignment into one string — the writer-mode check always printed 0/read-only EVEN IN WRITER MODE. The round-10 'fix' traded a fail-open race for an always-fail-open parser. Correct pattern for reading NUL-delimited /proc files fail-closed in shell: convert separators INSIDE the substitution with tr as the SOLE command — names=$(tr '\\0' '\\n' </proc/$pid/environ 2>/dev/null) && [ -n \"$names\" ] — redirect failure fails tr (a simple command, no pipe to mask it) AND newlines survive capture. Pair of lessons: (r10) never pipe after the read inside the substitution; (r11) never capture raw NUL data and transform after. (2) systemd Environment= supports quoted and multi-assignment forms (Environment=\"K=v\" FOO=bar K2=v2) — anchored '^Environment=[A-Z_]+' regex missed them; now split assignments and strip quotes (over-matching errs closed). (3) The clearing-drop-in recovery path dead-ended: UnsetEnvironment clears the effective env but the static preflight still flagged the unchanged EnvironmentFile → 'do NOT start' forever; preflight verdict now recognizes an active 'UnsetEnvironment=LOVYOU_API_KEY' drop-in as the sanctioned exception, with post-start /proc verification as authoritative proof. Round 12 running at head 26ae0e8742337c3129d81441baaa7b037ed9258b.

## 2026-07-11 · ??

[hive 138e9e5 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r12] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=138e9e5 — CFAR round-12 repairs (Codex reviewer, 2 P1 + 1 P2 accepted; FO v0.14.0 R7 ac-ae): (1+2) the restart sections' bounce-if-running branch executed `systemctl --user restart hive` unconditionally — but nucbuntu's packaged hive.service carries --approve-requests --approve-roles in ExecStart (verified in ~/.config/systemd/user/hive.service), so a plain 'hive restart' RESUMED FULL AUTONOMY without current-turn approval, and could resume production reconciliation if the unit's EnvironmentFile/manager env feeds LOVYOU_API_KEY. Branch now requires the credential preflight verdict AND greps effective ExecStart for --approve-(requests|roles), demanding explicit current-turn approval — the restart command itself became an echo'd instruction, never auto-executed. Standing-config lesson: 'do not ADD dangerous flags' does not protect against flags ALREADY BAKED INTO the unit — a restart re-launches whatever the unit encodes, so restart is as privileged as start-with-those-flags. (3) Stack tables falsely claimed loopback: compose publishes postgres '5432:5432' = ALL interfaces (dev credentials hive/hive network-exposed!) and work-server binds ':'+PORT = all interfaces; tables now state the real exposure. Possible future hardening issue: compose ports '127.0.0.1:5432:5432' — NOT authorized in this arc (would change runtime config). Round 13 running at head 138e9e5142251743f7778c97807a1ea5d28057b1.

## 2026-07-11 · ??

[hive 29b4a60 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r13] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=29b4a60 — CFAR round-13 repairs (Codex reviewer, 3 P1s accepted; FO v0.15.0 R7 af-ah): rebuilt the hive.service preflight on systemd's MERGED EFFECTIVE properties (`systemctl --user show hive -p Environment / -p EnvironmentFiles / -p UnsetEnvironment / -p ExecStart --value`) instead of text-parsing `systemctl cat` output. Class lesson worth keeping forever: NEVER regex-parse systemd unit text for authority/credential decisions — systemd's own config language defeats naive parsing three ways: (1) `Environment = 'K=v'` whitespace/single-quote forms miss exact-prefix greps; (2) list directives like UnsetEnvironment RESET when a later fragment sets them empty, so a raw directive line in `cat` output may be inactive; (3) drop-ins/fragments merge in ways only systemd resolves. `systemctl show -p X --value` returns the merged, normalized, effective value — parse THAT. Also: the autonomy-flag gate now runs before START too (was restart-only — asymmetric gating), via merged ExecStart. Preflight verdict now three-way: unreadable→do NOT start; credential-and-not-cleared→do NOT start; autonomy flags→explicit current-turn approval; else OK. Verified the snippet with bash -n. Round 14 running at head 29b4a600e2a40a45d6ae494792de13fcd8622dd1.

## 2026-07-11 · ??

[hive 6d5ebe0 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r14] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=6d5ebe0 — CFAR round-14 repairs (Codex reviewer, 2 P2s accepted; FO v0.16.0 R7 ai-aj): (1) `systemctl --user show-environment | cut | grep -qx` treated a FAILED show-environment read identically to 'credential absent' — pipeline head failure reads as no-match, the recurring fail-open shape; now the read is captured first (if mgrenv=$(...)) and failure sets unknown→do-NOT-start. (2) Inverse failure mode, wrongly-fail-closed: `systemctl show -p EnvironmentFiles --value` emits '(ignore_errors=…)' metadata tuples after EACH path; my sed anchored to $ stripped only the last, so multi-file units word-split intermediate tuples as 'filenames', found them unreadable, and blocked EVERY start — a fail-closed DoS of the runbook. Global sed //g fixes it. Note both directions matter in review: fail-open bugs breach authority; wrongly-fail-closed bugs make operators bypass the runbook entirely (alarm fatigue), which is its own safety failure. Round 15 running at head 6d5ebe087b3976d6e194232721553ccf11059426. This is a docs/runbook-only PR — 36 findings (a–aj) over 14 rounds, all in shell snippets and truth claims; the review long-tail is real but converging (rounds now yield 2 narrow P2s vs 5 P1s early).

[hive 1977edb 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r16] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=1977edb — CFAR round-16 repair (Codex reviewer, 1 P1 accepted; FO v0.18.0 R7 am): credential-injection blind spot — a systemd drop-in can launch the daemon through `/usr/bin/env LOVYOU_API_KEY=... <cmd>` or a shell wrapper, putting the production bearer in the COMMAND LINE rather than any environment source; the preflight scanned ExecStart only for autonomy flags, so this valid systemd form could get 'VERDICT: OK to start'. Critically, `UnsetEnvironment=` cannot clear an ExecStart-injected variable (it strips the environment block, not argv), so this case gets its own uncleearable do-NOT-start verdict branch (execcred) ranked above the drop-in-clearable branch in both dialects. ## 2026-07-11 · ??

[hive 717fc2b 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r17] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=717fc2b — CFAR round-17 repair (Codex reviewer, 1 P1 accepted; FO v0.19.0 R7 an): the terminal insight of the preflight arc — STRING-SCANNING HAS A FLOOR. A wrapper script referenced by ExecStart can source hive.env or append --approve-* flags inside its BODY, invisible to every systemd property check; scanning the merged ExecStart for bad substrings is a denylist that an opaque launcher defeats trivially. Final form is an ALLOWLIST of argv-transparent launchers: preflight extracts the ExecStart path= and accepts only */go or */hive (direct binaries whose full behavior is visible in argv); bash/sh/env/custom-script launchers → unknown → do NOT start, inspect the wrapper body manually. This closes the preflight's epistemic boundary honestly: analyze what is analyzable, refuse what is opaque — 'a string miss is not proof of safety' (Michael's allowlist-over-denylist doctrine landing in its purest form after 17 rounds). Round 18 running at head 717fc2b9877e00305459deeb10ca93d6e36b7f23.

## 2026-07-11 · ??

[hive f94c33e 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r18] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=f94c33e — CFAR round-18 repairs (Codex reviewer, 2 findings accepted; FO v0.20.0 R7 ao-ap): (1) allowlist-binding lesson: a suffix allowlist (*/hive, */go) is still spoofable — /tmp/hive passes */hive, and `go run /tmp/wrapper.go` passes */go. An allowlist over authority-relevant executables must bind to EXACT canonical identities: the built binary's absolute path, or go only when WorkingDirectory (merged property) is the hive repo AND argv contains 'go run ./cmd/hive'. (2) presence ≠ semantics: counting HIVE_OPS_HUMAN_ACTOR's presence over-claimed writer mode — cmd/hive-ops-api opsWriterOptions() returns read-only for BOTH empty and invalid actor ids (verified in source at main.go:113-122); probe now reads the value (operator actor id, not a secret), reports read-only when empty, and defers invalid-id judgment to the API's startup journal line. Meta-observation for the arc retro: 18 rounds of hardening a bash preflight suggests the runbook is nearing the wrong-tool boundary — a future slice could move the preflight into a tested Go subcommand (hive factory preflight) where TDD + the #266 harness patterns apply; will note as residual in the CFAR evidence. Round 19 running at head f94c33eb1d4216984ed394fc51ab8fb68f0d67df.

Multi-gate verdicts must enumerate EVERY blocker and demand each be individually resolved/authorized — first-match reporting turns stacked authorizations into single ones. (3) Config-precedence probe lesson: hive-ops-api's --catalog flag OVERRIDES HIVE_OPS_CATALOG (flag default = env value, cmd/hive-ops-api/main.go:27), so an env-only probe misreports when the flag is passed; probe now reads /proc/PID/cmdline first (same NUL-safe tr-sole-command pattern), env fallback, UNKNOWN on unreadable. [hive 2133042 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r23] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=2133042 — CFAR round-23 repairs (Codex reviewer, 2 P1s accepted; FO v0.25.0 R7 ay-az): (1) Go flag-syntax gotcha: the stdlib `flag` package treats `-approve-requests` and `--approve-requests` IDENTICALLY — any grep gating on the double-dash form alone misses the legal single-dash spelling; detection now matches `--?approve-(requests|roles)` with boundary anchors. (2) systemd `$VAR` expansion in ExecStart: `Environment=\"HIVE_FLAGS=--approve-requests\"` + `ExecStart=... $HIVE_FLAGS` expands ONLY at service start — `systemctl show -p ExecStart` exposes the unexpanded placeholder, so flags/credentials behind it were invisible while the canonical launcher passed. The recognized shape now rejects any `$` in the merged ExecStart (no variable expansion allowed). Both are instances of the same meta-rule: an allowlisted shape must exclude every INDIRECTION mechanism of the config language (wrappers, chained commands, aux phases, variable expansion, alternate flag spellings) — each indirection is a place authority can hide. [hive 339d273 2026-07-11 CFAR-267-r24] repo=transpara-ai/hive branch=feat/hive-265-lifecycle-skill-home PR=hive#267 commit=339d273 — CFAR round-24 repair (Codex reviewer, 1 P1 accepted; FO v0.26.0 R7 ba): anchoring lesson — the go-run target check `grep -q 'go run ./cmd/hive '` was an unanchored substring over the serialized argv, so `/snap/bin/go run ./cmd/wrapper.go --label \"go run ./cmd/hive\"` passed (the canonical text appearing as a LATER ARGUMENT satisfied the check while an opaque wrapper actually ran). Now the argv must BEGIN with the trusted launcher path itself followed by ' run ./cmd/hive': grep -qE \"^argv\\[\\]=$launcher run \\./cmd/hive( |$)\". General rule: identity checks over serialized command lines must anchor at position 0 and bind to the already-verified executable — substring presence anywhere is attacker-controllable data, not identity. ## 2026-07-11 · ??

[hive @ feat/hive-263-finalizer-guardrails, commit 34be5a0dee6e4acbcd7b93f383160455579e2527, 2026-07-11 marker OB-HIVE-272-R2] CFAR round 2 on transpara-ai/hive PR #272 (Codex gpt-5.6-sol) found 4 more P1s — all verified against the substrate before repair, all accepted-repaired in one class-sweep commit 34be5a0. (1) Non-human decider: my mark-ready lookup skipped the DeciderRole=="human" filter that the draft-PR path has — an operator/auto-generated authority.decision.recorded could satisfy a human-approval boundary. Fix: only human-decided records carry authority in EITHER direction (skip, don't refuse, so a non-human record can't shadow a human decision either). (2) Nonce consumption was per-ready-stage-task — two runs at the same repo/PR/head each consumed the same approval locally. Fix: global whole-store claim scan. (3) Check-then-append TOCTOU across processes. Fix: append-then-verify-winner — crypto/rand claim id per attempt; after append, re-scan; proceed only if own claim is OLDEST in the event chain's total order (no store-level CAS needed; exactly one concurrent claimant wins). (4) VERIFIED REAL: work TaskStore.ListArtifacts (work/store.go:1970) reads ONE newest-first page of 1000 ByType events — old consumption records/blocked evidence vanish under newer artifacts. Fix: authorization reads page the whole store via eventsByTypePaginated; proven by 1050-event burial test. Durable lesson: any authorization/terminality read over an event-sourced store must (a) page the WHOLE type, (b) filter for the authority-bearing role, (c) resolve concurrent claims by total event order, not check-then-act. FO v0.4.0. Round 3 running at 34be5a0.

## 2026-07-11 · ??

[hive @ feat/hive-263-finalizer-guardrails, commits 8f1e0febdbf2044fb95f5686d3515fd9027926a1 + 6d181af07e2eb6d7bd0a1544b21e5f96f685dced, 2026-07-11 marker OB-HIVE-272-R4R5] CFAR rounds 4 and 5 on transpara-ai/hive PR #272 (Codex gpt-5.6-sol reviewer). Round 4 (1 P1 + 3 P2, commit 8f1e0fe): (a) authority-currency re-check — approval resolved before consumption scans could go stale (expiry lapse, newer denial); fix: re-resolve the lookup AFTER consumption and require exact equality with the consumed approval before the GraphQL call; (b) same-run same-target consumption re-entry is idempotent so a transient evidence-recording failure after a successful flip can't strand the stage behind its own claim; (c) re-draft remediation under context.WithoutCancel + 60s timeout so caller cancellation can't disable the authorized safety cleanup; (d) malformed newest decisions REVOKE under latest-wins: attributable-and-matching fails the target closed, unattributable fails the whole gate closed. Round 5 (1 P1 + 1 P2, commit 6d181af): (a) MarkReadyForReview now returns a mutated bool — remediation only runs after a mutation THIS run performed; an already-ready PR on arrival records re_draft_not_attempted, never an un-flip of another actor's ready state (the approval covers the transition, not the state); (b) mutation-error reconcile uses the identity-only PR fetch — draft state, not CI health, proves non-mutation. RED for the reconcile fix observed by temporarily flipping the implementation back. FO now v0.7.0. Durable lessons: (1) an authority check is only as current as its distance from the side effect — re-validate immediately before mutating; (2) compensating actions need their own authority test: "may I undo?" is not implied by "may I do?" — never remediate state your run didn't create; (3) detach compensation from caller cancellation but keep it bounded; (4) idempotent re-entry must be scoped to same-actor same-transition, or retries strand; reuse protection must be scoped globally, or parallel runs replay. Round 6 running at 6d181af.

Architecture audit of the five TLC governance skills (TLC, IADA, CFADA, IAR, CFAR) filed as transpara-ai/platform#62 (repo: platform, no branch — issue only, no code change). Key findings: (1) Framing is correct as a four-layer system — skills for judgment, deterministic programs for fail-closed verification (Python operator tools in platform:tools/transpara-governance-gates + a Go gate state machine in work/pkg/worklifecycle), hooks as event tripwires, Codex plugin for distribution — but Claude side has no distribution layer (manual unversioned copy into ~/.claude/skills). The 2026-07-10 tlc-skill-reconciliation-record covered TLC only and its 'personal install is synced after merge' commitment re-broke within a day — no sync mechanism exists. (3) Civilization wiring is partial and parallel: work/pkg/worklifecycle carries GateIADA/GateCFADA/GateIAR/GateCFAR into hive's civilization assembly projection, eventgraph requires cfar_refs on production audit evidence, nine repos seed the cross-family-adversarial-review commit status; but the runtime never invokes the skills/gate tools, all 68 hive agent roles are gate-agnostic, no CI requires the status, and branch-protection enforcement is out-of-repo and unverified. Six numbered follow-ups are in the issue.
